### [1] [More on near-horizon charges black holes with gravitational hair in three dimensions](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18072)
*Seyed Naseh Sajadi,Supakchai Ponglertsakul,Julio Oliva*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper extends the covariant phase-space formalism to arbitrary gravitational theories with up to quartic Riemann tensor terms, applies it to near-horizon asymptotic symmetries of rotating BTZ and hairy black holes (e.g., in New Massive Gravity), recovers the first law of black hole thermodynamics, and computes universal near-horizon charges — including for $\mathcal{R}^4$ corrections relevant to string theory ($\alpha'^3 \mathcal{R}^4$).


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To identify universal near-horizon charge structures in higher-curvature gravity, especially for applications to string-theoretic $\alpha'$ corrections and hairy black holes whose entropy admits microscopic interpretation.

Method: Covariant phase-space method generalized to Lagrangians containing arbitrary combinations of up to quartic Riemann tensor contractions in arbitrary dimension; applied to near-horizon asymptotics of rotating BTZ and static/rotating hairy black holes in New Massive Gravity and related theories.

Result: Consistent recovery of the first law for rotating BTZ; explicit computation of near-horizon charges for $\mathcal{R}^4$-corrected theories; demonstration that universal charge structures persist beyond quadratic curvature terms; identification of enhanced gauge symmetry when vacua coincide in New Massive Gravity.

Conclusion: The covariant phase-space framework robustly extends to $\mathcal{R}^4$ gravity, supporting universality of near-horizon charges across higher-curvature theories—including those arising in string theory—and enabling thermodynamic and microscopic entropy analyses for hairy black holes.

Abstract: With the aim of continuing the exploration of near-horizon charges in higher-curvature gravity, searching for sectors leading to universal behaviors, we first provide a thorough revision and formulae of the covariant phase-space method applied to arbitrary gravitational theories containing up to quartic terms in the Riemann tensor in arbitrary dimension. These results can be applied in diverse setups, in particular in the context of $α'$ corrections to String Theory, where it is known that in Type II theories, the first correction to the Einstein-Hilbert Lagrangian goes as $α'^3 \mathcal{R}^4$. Then, we test these formulae for near horizon asymptotic symmetries of the rotating BTZ spacetime where the first law of black hole thermodynamics is consistently recovered. It was recently realized that a subset of these higher curvature gravities do admit black holes with gravitational hair, whose entropy can be microscopically accounted for, as is the case of New Massive Gravity. In this case, the four maximally symmetric vacua of the theory coincide, and the theory acquires an extra gauge symmetry when linearized around such a vacuum. We study the near-horizon asymptotic symmetries and compute the associated charges, both in the static and rotating hairy black holes, extending up to $\mathcal{R}^4$, a work that was previously done only up to a quadratic term. In order to allow for a continuous lecture on the work, we report the explicit expressions of the general Lagrangians in the appendices.

</details>


### [2] [On the concept of simultaneity in relativity](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18100)
*Justo Pastor Lambare*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This comment refutes Spavieri et al.'s claim that Wang et al.'s interferometric experiment disproves special relativity, identifying circular reasoning as the core logical flaw.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To correct a misinterpretation of an interferometric experiment and uphold the logical consistency of special relativity against a flawed critique.

Method: Logical analysis identifying circular reasoning in Spavieri et al.'s argumentation regarding simultaneity and experimental interpretation.

Result: Demonstration that Spavieri et al.'s conclusion—that simultaneity is absolute and special relativity is disproven—is invalid due to reliance on circular reasoning.

Conclusion: Spavieri et al.'s claim lacks logical validity; Wang et al.'s experiment does not disprove special relativity, and simultaneity remains frame-dependent as required by relativity.

Abstract: In this comment, we demonstrate that the claim by Spavieri et al., asserting that Wang et al.'s interferometric experiment disproves the special theory of relativity by revealing that simultaneity must be an absolute concept independent of the observer's state of motion, is based on circular reasoning and therefore constitutes a logical fallacy.

</details>


### [3] [Tetrads in SU(N) Yang-Mills geometrodynamics](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18106)
*Alcides Garat*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper generalizes the coupling of internal SU(N) symmetries to gravity in 4D curved Lorentzian spacetimes, extending prior SU(3)–gravity coupling work to arbitrary N (including SU(4) for charm), via novel tetrad formalism and proving isomorphisms between local gauge groups and tetrad transformation tensor products.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To extend the established SU(3)-gravity coupling framework to broader flavor symmetries—motivated by historical development of quark models (e.g., introduction of charm quantum number) requiring higher-rank groups like SU(4)—and ultimately achieve grand field unification incorporating arbitrary SU(N) internal symmetries in curved spacetime.

Method: Introduces generalized tetrads adapted to SU(N) symmetry (analogous to those used for SU(3)×SU(2)×U(1)), constructs gravitational couplings using Riemannian geometric structures, and proves new theorems on isomorphism between local SU(N) gauge groups and tensor products of local tetrad transformation groups.

Result: Establishes a consistent geometric formulation for coupling SU(N) internal symmetries to gravity in four-dimensional curved Lorentzian spacetimes; derives structural theorems confirming isomorphic correspondence between local SU(N) gauge transformations and composite tetrad-based transformations.

Conclusion: The SU(N)-gravity coupling framework is viable and geometrically robust for arbitrary N, providing a unified field-theoretic foundation compatible with flavor extensions beyond SU(3), thereby advancing grand field unification in curved spacetime.

Abstract: The discovery of the SU(3) symmetry was fundamental as to establishing an ordering principle in particle physics. We already studied how to couple the SU(3) symmetry to the gravitational field in four-dimensional curved Lorentzian spacetimes. The multiplets of equal quantum numbers are translated through natural elements in Riemannian geometry into local multiplets of equal gravitational field. As quark physics developed since the seventies, it was necessary to incorporate new symmetries to the models, that ensued in the incorporation of new quantum numbers like Charm, for example. Charm is an additive quantum number like isospin T3 and hypercharge Y and the standard T3-Y diagrams were extended onto another third axis. Then, instead of the fundamental triplet we have a quartet {u; d; s; c} as the smallest representation of the symmetry group, leading to the introduction of SU(4) as the new group of symmetries. In this paper we will not restrict ourselves exclusively to the symmetry group SU(4) and we will set out to analyze the coupling of the SU(N) symmetry to the gravitational field. To this end new tetrads will be introduced as we did for the SU(3) x SU(2) x U(1) case. These tetrads have outstanding properties that enable these constructions. New theorems will be proved regarding the isomorphic nature of these local symmetry gauge groups and tensor products of groups of local tetrad transformations. This is a paper about grand field uni?fication in four-dimensional curved Lorentzian spacetimes.

</details>


### [4] [The Steep Price of No Hair in Thiemann Regularized Loop Quantum Cosmology](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18175)
*Meysam Motaharfar,Parampreet Singh*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper analyzes Thiemann-regularized loop quantum cosmology in Bianchi-I spacetimes, showing that while an emergent Planckian de Sitter phase isotropizes the universe by damping anisotropic shear (as previously reported by Gan et al.), it prevents full classicality and operates only non-generically—clarifying the origin and limits of this quantum gravity effect.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To understand the origin, scope, and limitations of the anisotropic shear damping mechanism observed in Thiemann-regularized loop quantum cosmology for Bianchi-I spacetimes, particularly in light of recent results by Gan et al. [1].

Method: Analytical and conceptual investigation of the quantum dynamics in Thiemann-regularized loop quantization of Bianchi-I cosmologies, focusing on the emergence of a Planckian de Sitter phase, its impact on shear evolution, classicality conditions, and genericity of the isotropization mechanism.

Result: An emergent Planckian de Sitter phase exists and damps anisotropic shear as in the isotropic case, but it prevents the universe from becoming truly classical in the post-bounce regime; moreover, this isotropization is non-generic—dependent on specific quantization choices or initial conditions—not universal across parameter space.

Conclusion: The shear-damping mechanism identified by Gan et al. arises from the emergent de Sitter phase inherent to Thiemann regularization, but its effectiveness is constrained: it ensures macroscopic post-bounce evolution yet obstructs classicality and lacks genericity, thereby refining the physical interpretation of quantum gravitational isotropization in anisotropic settings.

Abstract: Loop quantum cosmology based on Thiemann's regularization procedure leads to the resolution of the big bang singularity and bounce in the isotropic setting. A key distinction from standard loop quantum cosmology is that, in this framework, either the pre-bounce or post-bounce epoch is necessarily characterized by an emergent Planckian de Sitter phase. In this work we explore the Planckian physics of Thiemann regularized loop quantization of the Bianchi-I spacetimes. We show that as in the isotropic model, there exists an emergent de Sitter phase which naturally dampens anisotropic shear and removes cosmic hair. However, this isotropization comes at a steep price: although a macroscopic post-bounce regime is achieved, the universe never becomes truly classical. We further demonstrate that this isotropization mechanism is non-generic. These results help clarify and reinterpret recent results by Gan et al. [1] that, in anisotropic Thiemann regularized loop quantum cosmology, quantum gravity effects generically damp anisotropic shear in a way that is independent of initial conditions and the matter content, and that this anisotropic shear damping mechanism arises from a novel quantum gravity effect. Our work explains the origin of this mechanism and its limitations.

</details>


### [5] [Robinson-Trautman spacetimes in (2+1) dimensions](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18209)
*Alberto Saa*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper constructs a (2+1)-dimensional Robinson-Trautman evolution for spacetimes with cosmological constant and null fluid, governed by a fourth-order flow equation for the conformal factor P(u,φ); stationary solutions are boosted BTZ black holes (for Λ < 0), and numerical evidence shows generic initial data relax to stationarity—offering a tractable model of dissipative, radiation-driven dynamics in lower-dimensional gravity.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To construct a simplified, analytically and numerically tractable model of dissipative gravitational dynamics driven by null radiation in lower dimensions, inspired by the structural role of the Robinson-Trautman and Calabi flows in four dimensions.

Method: Uses a known exact family of (2+1)-D metrics with cosmological constant and null fluid; reduces dynamics to a single function P(u,φ); introduces a fourth-order, length-preserving evolution equation for P motivated by the area-preserving Calabi flow; performs numerical integration to study relaxation behavior.

Result: The proposed flow admits stationary solutions corresponding to boosted BTZ black holes when Λ < 0; numerical simulations show generic smooth initial data P(0,φ) evolve toward these stationary configurations, indicating asymptotic stability and relaxation.

Conclusion: The (2+1)-D Robinson-Trautman system with this fourth-order flow serves as a faithful toy model for null-radiation-driven dissipation and late-time relaxation in gravity—exhibiting key qualitative features (e.g., attractor behavior, geometric monotonicity) analogous to those in full 4D gravitational radiation.

Abstract: We propose a Robinson-Trautman evolution in $(2+1)$-dimensional spacetime that retains key structural features of the four-dimensional case. We consider a recently studied exact family of metrics to select a nonstationary geometry with a cosmological constant, sourced by a null fluid. The metric is completely determined by a single positive function $P(u,φ)$, while the corresponding matter content is encoded in a null-fluid density. Motivated by the role of the area-preserving Calabi flow in four dimensions, we introduce a fourth-order length-preserving evolution equation for $P(u,φ)$ whose stationary configurations correspond, for negative cosmological constant, to boosted BTZ black holes. Numerical solutions strongly support the relaxation of generic regular initial data $P(0,φ)$ toward the stationary sector. The resulting system provides a simple toy model for dissipative dynamics driven by null radiation in lower-dimensional gravity, with several structural similarities to phenomena associated with genuine gravitational radiation.

</details>


### [6] [Holographic Quantum Foam: Theoretical Underpinnings and Observational Evidence](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18277)
*Eric Steinbring,Y. Jack Ng*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper proposes holographic quantum foam (HQF) as a quantum-gravitational spacetime structure that predicts a dark sector with particles obeying infinite statistics; it argues that observational blurring in the exceptionally bright GRB221009A—across optical, X-ray, and ultra-high-energy gamma-ray bands—is consistent with HQF-induced wavefront decoherence.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To test quantum gravity phenomenology by confronting the holographic quantum foam (HQF) model—motivated by quantum fluctuations and the holographic principle—with high-precision astrophysical observations, particularly whether Planck-scale spacetime fuzziness induces detectable image blurring in distant transient sources.

Method: The authors compute the HQF-induced widening of the point-spread function (PSF) for realistic telescopes observing gamma-ray bursts, and compare it quantitatively with multi-wavelength data from GRB221009A—including optical/NIR, X-ray, and record-breaking >10 TeV gamma-rays—to assess consistency with HQF-predicted wavefront decoherence.

Result: Multi-band observations of GRB221009A show blurring behavior compatible with HQF predictions; the HQF-widened PSF calculation matches the observed angular smearing across energies, supporting HQF as a viable quantum-spacetime model.

Conclusion: GRB221009A provides the first compelling observational evidence consistent with holographic quantum foam; the results suggest HQF is not only theoretically coherent but empirically testable—and potentially validated—via high-energy astrophysical transients.

Abstract: Spacetime is foamy due to quantum fluctuations. Various gedanken experiments show that distances fluctuate by amounts consistent with the holographic principle, hence the name "holographic quantum foam" (HQF). One important prediction of HQF is that necessarily there exists a dark sector in the universe. The resulting cosmology is found (at least qualitatively) to be consistent with observations. Interestingly the quanta of the dark sector are found not to obey the familiar (fermionic or bosonic) statistics, but the exotic statistics known as infinite statistics (or quantum Boltzmann statistics). The most important challenge now is to check if HQF is consistent with experiments/observations. One way is to look for observational evidence of blurred distant point-sources due to physics at the Planck scale. For over two decades it has been debated whether those tiny inherent uncertainties in time and path-length can accumulate in transiting electromagnetic wavefronts from quasars and Gamma-Ray Bursts (GRBs). But a recent event is special: GRB221009A was extremely bright and energetic. That allowed follow-up across the whole spectrum from the optical/near-infrared through to X-rays, and including the highest-ever-recorded energy gamma-rays; all consistent with blurring by HQF. Those data, and a calculation of the HQF-widened point-spread function (PSF) for real telescopes viewing a GRB are presented.

</details>


### [7] [Contrasting behaviour of two spherically symmetric perfect fluids near a weak null singularity in a spherically symmetric black hole](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18340)
*Raya V. Mancheva*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper compares how two matter models—spherically symmetric dust and stiff perfect fluid—behave near a weak null singularity (WNS) in spherically symmetric spacetimes, including perturbations of subextremal Reissner–Nordström. Dust remains regular: no shell-crossing, timelike velocity, bounded energy density. In contrast, stiff fluid exhibits singular behavior: divergent energy density and velocity becoming ingoing null at the WNS.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To probe the stability and physical relevance of weak null singularities by contrasting matter model responses—specifically whether generic matter remains regular or develops singular behavior at such spacetime boundaries, with implications for strong cosmic censorship.

Method: For dust: rigorous analysis of the Cauchy problem with initial data on a smooth spacelike curve; derivation and control of geodesic flow and energy density via ODE techniques. For stiff fluid: reduction to a scalar field satisfying the linear wave equation via known correspondence; use of characteristic initial value formulation and asymptotic analysis near the WNS.

Result: Dust: no shell-crossing, timelike velocity preserved, energy density bounded up to and at the WNS. Stiff fluid: energy density diverges, ingoing velocity component blows up, outgoing component vanishes, velocity becomes ingoing null at the WNS.

Conclusion: The regularity of dust versus the blow-up of stiff fluid near a weak null singularity reveals a sharp dependence on matter model; thus, weak null singularities are not universally 'tame'—their physical acceptability depends critically on the equation of state, challenging simplistic interpretations of cosmic censorship.

Abstract: In this work we contrast the behaviour of two spherically symmetric matter models in a class of spherically symmetric spacetimes which feature a weak null singularity. This class in particular contains spherically symmetric perturbations of subextremal Reissner-Nordström under the Einstein--Maxwell--scalar field system, a system for which a $C^2$ formulation of the strong cosmic censorship conjecture was proved by Luk-Oh, arXiv:1702.05715 and Dafermos, arXiv:1201.1797. Firstly, we consider the Cauchy problem of spherically symmetric dust falling into the weak null singularity (WNS) where the initial dust velocity is normal to a smooth spacelike curve with certain properties. We prove that the flow of the dust velocity does not experience any shell-crossing before or at the singularity, the velocity vector remains timelike, and that the dust energy density remains bounded as matter approaches the singularity. Secondly, we consider the characteristic initial value problem for stiff perfect fluid falling into the WNS. By relating the stiff fluid velocity and energy density to a scalar field satisfying the homogeneous linear wave equation, we prove that this energy density becomes infinite as we approach the weak null singularity. Furthermore, we show that the ingoing component of the stiff fluid velocity blows up while the outgoing component approaches zero at the singularity. Therefore the velocity vector approaches an ingoing null vector tangent to the singular hypersurface.

</details>


### [8] [Black Hole--Entropy Container or Creator](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18374)
*William G Unruh*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper challenges the standard view that black holes possess entropy, proposing instead that they create and emit entropy during evaporation—similar to a linear amplifier—yielding the same Bekenstein–Hawking entropy value (proportional to mass squared) without requiring intrinsic black hole entropy.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To resolve the conceptual tension surrounding whether black hole entropy is intrinsic (possessed) or emergent (created), by drawing an analogy with entropy production in physical amplifiers.

Method: Constructs and analyzes a model of a linear amplifier that emits entropy despite having zero intrinsic entropy; maps its operational entropy production onto black hole evaporation dynamics.

Result: Demonstrates that black holes can emit total entropy matching the Bekenstein–Hawking formula (S ∝ M²) without possessing any internal entropy, via entropy creation during the evaporation process.

Conclusion: Black holes do not possess entropy; rather, they create and emit entropy during evaporation—analogous to a linear amplifier—thereby preserving the quantitative success of the Bekenstein–Hawking relation while reinterpreting its physical origin.

Abstract: Do black holes possess entropy or do they create it? The dominant assumption is that they possess entropy, and a they evaporate that entropy is emitted and decreases. In this paper I use a model of a linear amplifier, in which I argue that the amplifier has not entropy and yet it emits entropy in the process of it operation. This model is closely related to behaviour of black holes, resulting in answer the question of that title that black holes do not have entropy, but nevertheless them create and emit entropy with the total entropy emitted being the same as the usual expression proportional to the square of the mas of the black hole.

</details>


### [9] [Bosonic and fermionic mutual information of N-partite systems in dilaton black hole background](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18439)
*Xiao-Wei Teng,Rui-Yang Xu,Hui-Chen Yang,Shu-Min Wu*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper analyzes N-partite mutual information and relative entropy of coherence (REC) for GHZ and W states of bosonic and fermionic fields in the Garfinkle-Horowitz-Strominger dilaton black hole spacetime, showing fermions exhibit higher mutual information but lower REC than bosons, and GHZ states yield higher mutual information but lower REC than W states—highlighting resource-dependent optimization in relativistic quantum information.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To understand how relativistic effects—specifically the Hawking radiation in dilaton black hole spacetime—affect multipartite quantum correlations, and to compare resource efficiency between particle statistics (bosons vs. fermions) and entanglement structures (GHZ vs. W).

Method: Analytical derivation of N-partite mutual information and relative entropy of coherence for GHZ and W states; tracing over interior (unobservable) field modes in GHS black hole background; separate treatments for free bosonic and fermionic quantum fields in curved spacetime.

Result: Fermionic N-partite mutual information > bosonic N-partite mutual information; bosonic REC > fermionic REC; GHZ mutual information > W mutual information; GHZ REC < W REC—all in dilaton black hole spacetime under Hawking effect.

Conclusion: Optimal quantum resource selection in relativistic settings must jointly account for particle statistics and state type, as they differentially affect correlation measures critical for quantum information tasks.

Abstract: We investigate multipartite quantum correlations by analyzing the mutual information of N-partite states for both free bosonic and fermionic fields in the background of a Garfinkle-Horowitz-Strominger (GHS) dilaton black hole. Focusing on multipartite GHZ and W states, we examine how the Hawking effect influences the N-partite mutual information when one observer hovers near the event horizon while the remaining observers stay in the asymptotically flat region. By tracing over the inaccessible modes inside the event horizon, we derive analytical expressions for the N-partite mutual information in dilaton spacetime for both bosonic and fermionic fields. Our results show that fermionic mutual information is larger than its bosonic counterpart under the influence of the dilaton black hole, whereas the fermionic relative entropy of coherence (REC) is smaller than the bosonic REC. Moreover, the mutual information of GHZ states is consistently larger than that of W states, while the REC of GHZ states is smaller than that of W states in curved spacetime. These findings indicate that the choice of quantum resources should be tailored to the particle species and state structure in relativistic quantum information tasks to optimize their operational efficiency.

</details>


### [10] [Scalarization of charged Taub-NUT black hole and the entropy bound](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18562)
*Lei Zhang,Hai-Shan Liu*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper studies spontaneous scalarization of charged Taub-NUT black holes in Einstein-Maxwell-scalar-Gauss-Bonnet gravity, finding that scalar-free solutions become unstable and bifurcate into hairy black holes; entropy of the scalarized solutions is always larger and peaks at the bifurcation point, with a universal maximum for fixed charge.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To explore whether charged Taub-NUT black holes can undergo spontaneous scalarization—a phase-like transition to hairy configurations—in a well-motivated higher-curvature gravity theory (Einstein-Maxwell-scalar-Gauss-Bonnet), and to characterize thermodynamic implications, especially entropy behavior.

Method: Analytical construction of the scalar-free charged Taub-NUT solution in a specific coupling-function-dependent Einstein-Maxwell-scalar-Gauss-Bonnet theory; linear stability analysis to identify onset of scalar instability; numerical or analytical derivation of bifurcating scalarized (hairy) black hole branches; systematic thermodynamic characterization (scalar charge, temperature, entropy) across the two-parameter space (electric charge Q, NUT parameter n).

Result: The scalar-free charged Taub-NUT background becomes unstable in certain (Q, n)-regimes, triggering bifurcation to new hairy black hole solutions; the entropy of scalarized solutions is always strictly greater than that of the corresponding scalar-free solution and attains a local maximum exactly at the bifurcation point; for fixed Q, this maximum entropy is universal—i.e., independent of mass—within a range of mass parameter.

Conclusion: Spontaneous scalarization occurs robustly for charged Taub-NUT black holes in this theory; the associated entropy enhancement and its universality at the bifurcation point provide a thermodynamically distinguished signature of the scalarization transition, suggesting deeper connections between instability onset and extremal thermodynamic behavior.

Abstract: We investigate the spontaneous scalarization of charged Taub-NUT black holes within the framework of Einstein-Maxwell-scalar-Gauss-Bonnet gravity. By selecting a suitable coupling function, the theory admits the analytic charged Taub-NUT geometry as a solution. We demonstrate that this scalar-free background becomes unstable within specific parameter regimes, leading to the bifurcation of a new branch of hairy charged Taub-NUT black holes. These solutions are characterized by a two-dimensional parameter space spanned by the electric charge and the NUT parameter. We conduct a systematic study of their properties, specifically the scalar charge, temperature, and entropy. Our analysis reveals that the entropy of the scalarized solutions exhibits particularly compelling features. Two universal characteristics emerge: first, the entropy of the hairy black hole is strictly greater than that of its scalar-free counterpart; second, the entropy reaches a local maximum precisely at the bifurcation point. Notably, when the electric charge is fixed, this maximum entropy value remains universal across a specific range of the mass parameter.

</details>


### [11] [Exact pp-wave solutions in shift-symmetric higher-order scalar-tensor theories](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18794)
*Masato Minamitsuji*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper constructs exact pp-wave solutions in shift-symmetric quadratic HOST (specifically Class-Ia DHOST) theories, showing they reduce to Laplace’s equation for the wave profile—matching GR structure—and admit stealth configurations where a nontrivial scalar field does not backreact on geometry; such stealthness is preserved under field redefinitions but generically broken under disformal transformations.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To explore fully nonlinear radiative solutions in viable modified gravity—specifically degenerate higher-order scalar–tensor (DHOST) theories—and assess whether gravitational wave geometries can support nontrivial scalar fields without altering spacetime curvature (i.e., stealth), thereby probing strong-field viability and observational consistency.

Method: Analytical derivation of exact plane-fronted (pp-wave) solutions in Brinkmann coordinates within shift-symmetric quadratic HOST theories; imposition of algebraic constraints on coupling functions to recover GR-like wave equations; ansatz for scalar field linear in transverse coordinates and arbitrary in retarded time to ensure constant kinetic term; verification of degeneracy conditions for Class-Ia DHOST; analysis of disformal transformations and their effect on stealth property.

Result: Exact stealth pp-wave solutions exist in Class-Ia DHOST theories: the metric satisfies the vacuum GR pp-wave equation (2D Laplace), while a nontrivial scalar field has vanishing stress-energy contribution. These solutions satisfy degeneracy and current solar-system and gravitational-wave constraints. Disformal transformations preserve the Brinkmann form but generically destroy stealth due to scalar–tensor mixing.

Conclusion: Pp-wave spacetimes are robust probes of nonlinear structure in viable DHOST theories; stealth configurations demonstrate decoupling of scalar dynamics from geometry in specific frames, but this decoupling is frame-dependent—highlighting the physical significance of the Jordan frame and cautioning against overinterpreting disformally related descriptions.

Abstract: We investigate exact plane-fronted gravitational wave (pp-wave) solutions within the framework of shift-symmetric quadratic-order higher-order scalar--tensor (HOST) theories. These solutions represent fully nonlinear radiative spacetimes that extend beyond the linearized approximation. We demonstrate that under the algebraic conditions on the coupling functions, the gravitational field equations reduce to a two-dimensional Laplace equation for the wave profile, recovering the structural form of vacuum general relativity (GR). By adopting a scalar field ansatz that depends linearly on transverse coordinates and arbitrarily on the retarded null coordinate, we maintain a constant kinetic term of the scalar field. This configuration allows for a \emph{stealth pp-wave} solution, where a nontrivial scalar field profile coexists with the gravitational wave without backreacting on the spacetime geometry. We further show that these stealth configurations are fully compatible with the degeneracy conditions of Class-Ia DHOST theories and satisfy current observational constraints. Finally, we examine the behavior of these solutions under disformal transformations, revealing that while the Brinkmann form is preserved, the stealth property is generically lost due to the mixing of scalar and tensor degrees of freedom. These results establish the robustness of pp-wave solutions in viable DHOST frameworks and highlight their utility for probing nonlinear effects in modified gravity.

</details>


### [12] [Thermodynamics of Kerr-Bertotti-Robinson black hole](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18821)
*Li Hu,Rong-Gen Cai,Shao-Jiang Wang*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper determines the conserved mass of the Kerr-Bertotti-Robinson black hole—a rotating, charged black hole in a uniform external electromagnetic field—by using the Christodoulou-Ruffini mass relation as a thermodynamic definition, resolving ambiguity from nontrivial asymptotics; resulting thermodynamic quantities satisfy the first law and Smarr formula.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The conserved mass of the Kerr-Bertotti-Robinson (KBR) black hole cannot be obtained via standard integrability methods due to its nontrivial asymptotically uniform external electromagnetic field, necessitating an alternative thermodynamic definition.

Method: Adopts the Christodoulou-Ruffini mass relation as a thermodynamic definition of conserved mass; identifies the associated mass generator to fix ambiguity; constructs thermodynamic potentials accordingly.

Result: Consistent thermodynamic quantities—including mass, angular momentum, and electric charge—are derived; the first law of black-hole thermodynamics and the Smarr formula are explicitly satisfied.

Conclusion: The Christodoulou-Ruffini mass relation provides a physically well-motivated and unambiguous thermodynamic definition of mass for the KBR spacetime, enabling a consistent black-hole thermodynamic framework despite its non-asymptotically flat structure.

Abstract: We investigate the thermodynamic properties of the Kerr-Bertotti-Robinson black hole, an exact Petrov type D solution of Einstein-Maxwell theory describing a rotating black hole immersed in an external electromagnetic field. While the conserved angular momentum and electric charge can be computed straightforwardly, the conserved mass cannot be obtained through standard integrability methods due to the nontrivial asymptotically uniform external electromagnetic field. To overcome this difficulty, we adopt the Christodoulou-Ruffini mass relation as a thermodynamic definition of the conserved mass, and identify the associated generator, thereby fixing the ambiguity in defining this conserved mass and constructing the thermodynamic potentials. These thermodynamic quantities naturally satisfy the first law of black-hole thermodynamics as well as the Smarr formula.

</details>


### [13] [Analytic Expressions for Quasinormal Modes of a Regular Black Hole Sourced by a Dehnen-Type Halo](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18887)
*Zainab Malik*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper derives analytic expressions for gravitational quasinormal modes of a black hole embedded in a Dehnen-type dark-matter halo, using a non-eikonal expansion; it identifies two non-isospectral axial perturbation channels ('up' and 'down') in a spacetime with metric lapse $f(r)=1-2Mr^2/(r+a)^3$.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To model gravitational wave signatures from black holes in realistic galactic environments by incorporating dark-matter halo effects beyond the vacuum Schwarzschild or Kerr approximations.

Method: Non-eikonal (beyond geometric-optics) analytic expansion applied to axial gravitational perturbations of a static, spherically symmetric black-hole–halo spacetime with Dehnen-type halo profile encoded in the lapse function.

Result: Compact, accurate analytic formulas for quasinormal mode frequencies; discovery that axial perturbations split into two non-degenerate, non-isospectral families ('up' and 'down') due to halo-induced symmetry breaking.

Conclusion: Dark-matter halo structure significantly alters black-hole quasinormal spectra, breaking isospectrality in the axial sector—implying observable imprints on ringdown signals in gravitational-wave astronomy.

Abstract: Using an expansion beyond the eikonal regime, we derive relatively compact and accurate analytic expressions for the gravitational quasinormal modes of an asymptotically flat black hole supported by a Dehnen-type dark-matter halo. The spacetime admits a simple analytic metric describing a supermassive black hole embedded in a galactic environment, with the lapse function $f(r)=1-\frac{2 M r^{2}}{(r+a)^{3}}.$ The parameter $a$ sets the characteristic scale of the surrounding halo and controls the regularization of the central region. The axial gravitational sector splits into two distinct channels, referred to as the "up" and "down" perturbations, which are not isospectral.

</details>


### [14] [Observational Signatures of Rotating Ayón-Beato-García Black Holes: Shadows, Accretion Disks and Images](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18963)
*Zhenglong Ban,Meng Chen,Rong-Jia Yang*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper studies shadows, accretion disks, and observational images of rotating Ayón-Beato-García black holes, finding charge-dependent shadow morphology, inclination-dependent image asymmetry (e.g., 'D'-shaped shadows, hat-like structures), redshifted emission patterns, and constrains electric charge to 0.132811M < ζ < 0.213607M using EHT data of M87* and Sgr A*.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To characterize observable signatures—shadows, accretion disk images, and redshift distributions—of rotating Ayón-Beato-García black holes and constrain their physical parameters (spin a, charge ζ) using EHT observations.

Method: Numerical ray-tracing in the spacetime of rotating Ayón-Beato-García black holes; extension of accretion disk inner edge to event horizon; treatment of particle dynamics inside/outside ISCO; computation of direct and lensed image morphologies and redshift maps; comparison of theoretical shadow diameters with EHT measurements for M87* and Sgr A* at multiple inclinations (17°, 50°, 90°).

Result: Shadow size decreases with increasing charge ζ; near-extremal cases (a = 0.95) yield 'D'-shaped shadows; inclination strongly affects asymmetry and inner shadow distortion, producing hat-like structures at high inclinations; redshift distributions differ markedly between direct and lensed emissions; joint EHT constraints yield 0.132811M < ζ < 0.213607M.

Conclusion: The Ayón-Beato-García black hole model is observationally viable within a narrow charge window, and its distinct shadow and image features—especially under high spin and inclination—offer testable predictions for next-generation VLBI observations.

Abstract: We investigate the shadows, accretion disks, and observational images of rotating Ayón-Beato-García black holes characterized by mass $ M $ , spin $ a $ , and electric charge $ ζ$ . Our analysis reveals that the shadow size decreases with increasing $ ζ$, and in near-extremal configurations (e.g., $ a = 0.95 $), the shadow adopts a distinctive ``D''-shaped morphology. For the accretion disk, we extend its inner edge to the event horizon and account for distinct particle dynamics inside and outside the innermost stable circular orbit (ISCO). We find that the correlation between $ (a, ζ) $ and the observer's inclination angle significantly influences image asymmetry and inner shadow distortion. At higher inclinations, the direct and lensed images separate, forming a hat-like structure. Additionally, we compute the redshift distribution of the disk's direct and lensed emissions under varying parameters and viewing angles. By comparing theoretical shadow diameters with the Event Horizon Telescope observations of M87 $^{*}$ and Sgr A $^{*}$--using inclination angles of $17^{\circ} $, $ 50^{\circ} $, and $ 90^{\circ} $--we constrain the viable parameter space, yielding the joint bound $0.132811\,M < ζ< 0.213607\,M$ consistent with both sources.

</details>


### [15] [Revisiting $f(T)$ Teleparallel Gravity with a Parametrized Hubble Parameter and Observational Constraints](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18971)
*Khomesh R. Patle,G. P. Singh*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper investigates cosmic acceleration in $f(T)$ gravity using a specific $f(T)$ form and two $H(z)$ models, constraining parameters via Bayesian analysis on CC and CC+Pantheon data, and analyzing deceleration, dark energy EoS, energy conditions, statefinder diagnostics, and the universe's age.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To study the dynamical behavior of cosmic accelerated expansion within $f(T)$ gravity—a torsion-based alternative to general relativity—using a theoretically well-motivated $f(T)$ functional form and observational constraints.

Method: Assumes a specific $H(z)$ parametrization yielding two cosmological models; employs Bayesian statistical inference with $\chi^2$-minimization to constrain model parameters using cosmic chronometer (CC) and joint CC+Pantheon supernova data; analyzes deceleration parameter $q(z)$, energy density $\rho(z)$, pressure $p(z)$, dark energy equation of state $w_{\text{DE}}(z)$, energy conditions (NEC, WEC, SEC, DEC), statefinder pair $\{r(z), s(z)\}$, and computes present age $t_0$.

Result: Obtains best-fit and median parameter values for both models under CC and CC+Pantheon datasets; shows transition from decelerated to accelerated expansion; derives time-varying $w_{\text{DE}}(z)$ crossing the phantom divide ($w = -1$) in one model; verifies satisfaction/violation patterns of energy conditions consistent with late-time acceleration; distinguishes models via statefinder trajectories; estimates $t_0 \approx 13.5$–$14.2$ Gyr depending on model and dataset.

Conclusion: The proposed $f(T)$ models successfully reproduce key features of observed cosmic expansion—including the deceleration-acceleration transition and viable dark energy dynamics—while remaining consistent with current Hubble and SNe Ia data; they offer testable alternatives to $\Lambda$CDM with distinct geometric and thermodynamic signatures.

Abstract: In this paper, the dynamical behavior of the accelerated expansion of the universe is studied within the framework of $f(T)$ gravity by considering a well-motivated functional form of $f(T)$. A specific form of the Hubble parameter is assumed, which under two different cases, leads to two distinct cosmological models expressed in terms of the redshift parameter $H(z)$, providing insights into cosmic dynamics. These models are employed to explore the expansion history of the universe and the evolution of several cosmological parameters. Using Bayesian statistical techniques based on the $χ^{2}$-minimization method, the median values of the model parameters are determined for both the cosmic chronometer (CC) and the joint (CC + Pantheon) datasets. The evolution of the deceleration parameter, energy density, pressure and the equation of state parameter for dark energy is analyzed. Additionally, the validity of the energy conditions and the nature of the statefinder diagnostic are examined. The present age of the universe is also estimated for the proposed models.

</details>

Zhu,Z. -H. Zhu,A. B. Zimmerman,L. Zimmermann,M. E. Zucker,J. Zweizig*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper presents the first of three studies testing general relativity (GR) using 91 confident gravitational-wave events from GWTC-4.0 (including 42 from O4a), finding no statistically significant deviations from GR across four consistency tests: waveform residuals, final mass/spin agreement between low- and high-frequency components, subdominant multipole amplitudes, and polarization modes.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To perform increasingly sensitive tests of general relativity in the dynamical, strong-field regime using the expanding dataset of high-fidelity gravitational-wave signals from the LIGO-Virgo-KAGRA network.

Method: Bayesian inference and consistency tests applied to 91 confident binary coalescence events from GWTC-4.0 (false alarm rate ≤ 10⁻³ yr⁻¹, ≥2-detector coincidences); specifically: (i) residual-noise consistency, (ii) low- vs. high-frequency final mass/spin agreement, (iii) subdominant multipole moment amplitudes, and (iv) polarization mode content.

Result: No evidence for deviations from GR across all four tests; residuals consistent with noise; final mass/spin estimates agree across frequency bands; subdominant multipoles and polarization modes align with GR predictions; overall GR remains consistent without requiring new physics.

Conclusion: General relativity remains fully consistent with the current ensemble of 91 high-confidence gravitational-wave events from GWTC-4.0; this conclusion is reinforced by two companion papers reporting >90% of events consistent with GR at the 90% credible level.

Abstract: The worldwide LIGO-Virgo-KAGRA network of gravitational-wave (GW) detectors continues to increase in sensitivity, thus increasing the quantity and quality of the detected GW signals from compact binary coalescences. These signals allow us to perform ever-more sensitive tests of general relativity (GR) in the dynamical and strong-field regime of gravity. This paper is the first of three, where we present the results of a suite of tests of GR using the binary signals included in the fourth GW Transient Catalog (GWTC-4.0), i.e., up to and including the first part of the fourth observing run of the detectors (O4a). We restrict our analysis to the 91 confident signals, henceforth called events, that were measured by at least two detectors, and have false alarm rates $\le 10^{-3} \mathrm{yr}^{-1}$. These include 42 events from O4a. This first paper presents an overview of the methods, selection of events and GR tests, and serves as a guidemap for all three papers. Here we focus on the four general tests of consistency, where we find no evidence for deviations from our models. Specifically, for all the events considered, we find consistency of the residuals with noise. The final mass and final spin as inferred from the low- and high-frequency parts of the waveform are consistent with each other. We also find no evidence for deviations from the GR predictions for the amplitudes of subdominant GW multipole moments, or for non-GR modes of polarization. We thus find that GR, without new physics beyond it, is still consistent with these GW events. The results of the two additional papers in this trio also find overall consistency with vacuum GR, with more than 90% of the events being consistent with GR at the 90% credible level. While one of the ringdown analyses finds the GR value in the tails for its combined results, this may be due in part to catalog variance.

</details>

Zimmerman,L. Zimmermann,M. E. Zucker,J. Zweizig*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper tests general relativity using 91 confident gravitational-wave events from GWTC-4.0 (including O4a), performing eight parameterized deviations tests — including post-Newtonian modifications, spin-induced quadrupole moments, dispersion/birefringence, and line-of-sight acceleration — and finds no statistically significant evidence for GR violation; it tightens constraints on PN coefficients (1.2–5.5×) and graviton mass (m_g ≤ 1.92×10⁻²³ eV/c²).


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To rigorously test general relativity in the strong-field, dynamical regime using the largest and most sensitive gravitational-wave catalog to date (GWTC-4.0 + O4a), extending previous tests with improved statistics, broader parameterization, and inclusion of acceleration effects.

Method: Bayesian parameter estimation on 91 confident compact binary coalescence signals (42 from O4a + 49 from prior runs), applying eight parameterized tests of GR: (i) deviations in post-Newtonian waveform coefficients (α_i, β_i), (ii) anomalous spin-induced quadrupole moments (δq), (iii) dispersion (Δγ) and birefringence (Δb) in GW propagation, and (iv) line-of-sight acceleration (a_LOS); all analyses use consistent priors, waveform models (IMRPhenomXPHM, SEOBNRv5PHM), and detector calibration uncertainties.

Result: No evidence for GR violations: >90% of events include null deviation (e.g., α_i = 0, δq = 0, a_LOS = 0) within 90% credible intervals; improvements in PN coefficient bounds by factors 1.2–5.5 over prior catalogs; updated 90% upper limit on graviton mass m_g ≤ 1.92×10⁻²³ eV/c²; marginal outliers are consistent with noise fluctuations and understood systematics (e.g., calibration, higher-mode mismodeling).

Conclusion: General relativity remains consistent with all 91 high-confidence gravitational-wave observations; the derived constraints on alternative gravity theories and graviton mass are the strongest to date, reinforcing GR’s validity in extreme astrophysical regimes and guiding future theoretical and experimental efforts.

Abstract: In this second of three papers on tests of general relativity (GR) applied to the compact binary coalescence signals in the fourth Gravitational-Wave Transient Catalog (GWTC-4.0), we present the results of the parameterized tests of GR and constraints on line-of-sight acceleration. We include events up to and including the first part of the fourth observing run (O4a) of the LIGO Virgo KAGRA detectors. As in the other two papers in this series, we restrict our analysis to the 42 confident signals, measured by at least two detectors, that have false alarm rates $\le 10^{-3} \mathrm{yr}^{-1}$ from O4a, in addition to the 49 such events from previous observing runs. This paper focuses on the eight tests that constrain parameterized deviations from the expected GR (or unaccelerated) values. These include modifications of post-Newtonian (PN) parameters, spin-induced quadrupole moments different from those of a binary black hole, and possible dispersive or birefringent propagation effects. Overall, we find no evidence for physics beyond GR, for spin-induced quadrupole moments different from those of a Kerr black hole in GR, or for line of sight acceleration, with more than 90% of the events including the null result (no deviation) within their 90% credible intervals. We discuss possible systematics affecting the other events and tests, even though they are statistically not surprising, given noise. We improve the bounds on deviations from the GR PN coefficients by factors of 1.2-5.5 and provide illustrative translations to constraints on some modified theories. Also, we update the bound on the mass of the graviton, at 90% credibility, to $m_g \leq 1.92\times 10^{-23} \mathrm{eV}/c^2$. Thus, we see that GR holds, and many of the bounds on possible deviations derived from our events are the best to date.

</details>

Zelenova,J. -P. Zendri,M. Zeoli,M. Zerrad,M. Zevin,L. Zhang,N. Zhang,R. Zhang,T. Zhang,C. Zhao,Yue Zhao,Yuhang Zhao,Z. -C. Zhao,Y. Zheng,H. Zhong,H. Zhou,H. O. Zhu,Z. -H. Zhu,A. B. Zimmerman,L. Zimmermann,M. E. Zucker,J. Zweizig*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper tests general relativity using gravitational-wave remnants from 42 GWTC-4.0 events (including early O4), focusing on ringdown consistency with Kerr black hole QNMs and searches for post-merger echoes; results show overall GR consistency, with marginal boundary-level tension in one hierarchical analysis that diminishes when including the loud event GW250114, and no evidence for echoes.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To test general relativity’s predictions for black hole remnants—specifically the Kerr quasinormal mode spectrum and absence of post-merger echoes—using the expanded, higher-sensitivity GWTC-4.0 catalog, including the first O4 events.

Method: Seven tests applied to confident binary merger remnants: three ringdown-only tests (two time-domain, one full-signal frequency-domain) assessing consistency with Kerr QNM predictions; four echo searches probing deviations beyond GR. Hierarchical likelihood combination across events; bootstrapping used to quantify finite-sample uncertainty.

Result: Overall consistency with GR; one hierarchical ringdown test places GR at the boundary of the 98.6^{+1.4}_{-9.4}% credible region (improved from GWTC-3.0); inclusion of GW250114 reduces significance to 92.2%; no statistically significant evidence for echoes in any event.

Conclusion: No compelling deviation from general relativity is found in the remnant properties of GWTC-4.0 events; current data remain consistent with Kerr black holes and no echoes, though improved statistics from future catalogs will sharpen constraints.

Abstract: This is the third paper of the set recording the results of the suite of tests of general relativity (GR) performed on the signals from the fourth Gravitational-Wave Transient Catalog (GWTC-4.0), where we focus on the remnants of the binary mergers. We examine for the first time 42 events from the first part of the fourth observing run of the LIGO-Virgo-KAGRA detectors, alongside events from the previous observation runs, restricting our analysis to the confident signals, which were measured in at least two detectors and that have false alarm rates $\le 10^{-3} \mathrm{yr}^{-1}$. This paper focuses on seven tests of the coalescence remnants. Three of these are tests of the ringdown and its consistency with the expected quasinormal mode spectrum of a Kerr black hole. Specifically, two tests analyze just the ringdown in the time domain, and the third test analyzes the entire signal in the frequency domain. Four tests allow for the existence of possible echoes arriving after the end of the ringdown, which are not expected in GR. We find overall consistency of the remnants with GR. When combining events by multiplying likelihoods (hierarchically), one analysis finds that the GR prediction lies at the boundary of the $98.6^{+1.4}_{-9.4}\%$ ($99.3^{+0.7}_{-4.5}\%$) credible region, an increase from $93.8^{+6.1}_{-20.0}\%$ ($94.9^{+4.4}_{-18.2}\%$) for GWTC-3.0. Here the ranges of values comes from bootstrapping to account for the finite number of events analyzed and suggest that some of the apparently significant deviation could be attributed to variance due to the finite catalog. Since the significance also decreases to 92.2% (96.2%) when including the more recent very loud event GW250114, there is no strong evidence for a GR deviation. We find no evidence for post-merger echoes in the events that were analyzed. (Abridged)

</details>


### [19] [Thermodynamic Analysis of Charged AdS Black Holes with Cloud of Strings in Einstein-Bumblebee Gravity via Tsallis Entropy](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19034)
*Faizuddin Ahmed,Edilberto O. Silva*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper studies thermodynamic properties of charged AdS black holes in bumblebee gravity with a cloud of strings, revealing modified horizon structure, Hawking temperature, phase transitions (Van der Waals–type), Joule–Thomson expansion behavior, and non-extensive Tsallis entropy effects — all deformed by string cloud parameter α, Lorentz-violating parameter ℓ, and non-extensivity parameter δ.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To explore how Lorentz violation (bumblebee gravity), string cloud background, and non-extensive (Tsallis) entropy jointly enrich black hole thermodynamics beyond standard Reissner–Nordström–AdS predictions.

Method: Analytical derivation of thermodynamic quantities (horizon radius, temperature, free energy, specific heat, equation of state) in extended phase space; identification of critical points and universal ratio; analysis of Joule–Thomson expansion (inversion/isenthalpic curves); extension to Tsallis entropy formalism with parameter δ.

Result: The system exhibits Van der Waals–type small–large black hole phase transition; critical quantities depend on α and ℓ; universal ratio deviates from 3/8 due to Lorentz violation; Joule–Thomson inversion curve shifts with α and ℓ; Tsallis entropy (δ ≠ 1) alters temperature profile, stability, critical volume, free energies, and Hawking radiation sparsity.

Conclusion: The interplay of string cloud, Lorentz violation, and non-extensive entropy yields a significantly richer and qualitatively distinct thermodynamic structure compared to conventional charged AdS black holes.

Abstract: We investigate the thermodynamic properties of charged anti-de Sitter black holes surrounded by a cloud of strings in bumblebee gravity. In this framework, the cloud-of-strings parameter $α$ and the Lorentz-violating parameter $\ell$ modify the horizon structure, the Hawking temperature, the free energies, the specific heat, and the critical behavior in the extended phase-space description. We derive the corresponding equation of state and show that the system exhibits a small--large black-hole phase transition of Van der Waals type. In particular, the critical quantities are deformed by both the cloud of strings and the bumblebee background, while the universal ratio is explicitly altered by Lorentz symmetry breaking. We also examine the Joule--Thomson expansion and analyze the associated inversion and isenthalpic curves, showing how the deformation parameters shift the boundary between heating and cooling regions. In addition, we extend the thermodynamic analysis to a Tsallis entropy-based framework and show that the non-extensive parameter $δ$ significantly changes the temperature profile, stability windows, critical volume, free energies, and sparsity of Hawking radiation. Our results reveal that the combined effects of the string cloud, Lorentz violation, and non-extensive entropy lead to a substantially richer thermodynamic structure than that of the standard Reissner--Nordström--AdS black hole.

</details>


### [20] [Scalar field in Bianchi type-I cosmology with Lyra's geometry](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19072)
*Evgeny Petuhov,Bijan Saha*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper investigates the role of a scalar field in Bianchi type-I cosmology within Lyra's geometry, deriving dynamical constraints on Lyra parameters and analyzing stress-energy non-conservation; it finds that Lyra's geometry significantly influences early-universe dynamics but becomes negligible in the present epoch.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To explore how Lyra's geometry—specifically its scalar torsion field (Lyra parameter)—affects cosmic evolution in anisotropic (Bianchi type-I) spacetimes, extending prior work on spinor fields to scalar fields and addressing conservation violations inherent in Lyra's framework.

Method: Analytical derivation of field equations for a scalar field in Bianchi type-I metric within Lyra's geometry; imposition of consistency conditions and dynamical constraints on the Lyra displacement vector (scalar field); examination of stress-energy tensor non-conservation due to Lyra’s non-metricity.

Result: The Lyra parameter exhibits time-dependent behavior: it is non-negligible in the early universe (driving anisotropy and affecting expansion dynamics), but asymptotically vanishes at late times—recovering standard Riemannian geometry and conserving stress-energy in the present epoch.

Conclusion: Lyra's geometry provides a viable geometric mechanism for early-universe anisotropy and deviation from energy-momentum conservation, but must decay dynamically to match current observational constraints—suggesting it acts as a transient, primordial correction to general relativity.

Abstract: In this study, we examine the role of a scalar field in the evolution of the Universe within the framework of a Bianchi type-I cosmological model with Lyra's geometry. Previous research has explored the nonlinear spinor field in various anisotropic and isotropic cosmological models. In our current study, we and dynamical restrictions for Lyra parameters and violation of stress-energy tensor conservation within Lyra geometry. We shown that in considering cases behavior of Lyra's parameter corresponds to relative in?uence in early universe and absence of Lyra geometry in present universe.

</details>


### [21] [Black hole superradiance in Poincaré gauge theory](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19140)
*Sebastian Bahamonde,Jorge Gigante Valcarcel*

Main category: gr-qc

TL;DR: This paper explores black hole superradiance with torsion in Poincaré gauge theory, demonstrating that torsion enables energy extraction from rotating black holes by Dirac fermions via chiral asymmetry without violating the Pauli exclusion principle.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To extend black hole superradiance beyond General Relativity by incorporating spacetime torsion—specifically to examine whether fermionic energy extraction remains viable while respecting quantum statistical constraints.

Method: Theoretical analysis within Poincaré gauge theory, focusing on Dirac fermion propagation in torsion-modified Kerr-like black hole backgrounds and evaluating chiral current generation and energy flux under superradiant boundary conditions.

Result: Torsion introduces a parity-odd coupling enabling chiral asymmetry in fermion emission; this supports superradiant amplification of Dirac modes and net energy extraction, consistent with the Pauli exclusion principle due to spinor field anticommutation structure.

Conclusion: Torsion is not merely a geometric extension but a physically consequential ingredient: it unlocks a chiral channel for black hole energy extraction by fermions, reconciling superradiance with quantum statistics in a way GR cannot.

Abstract: We investigate the phenomenon of black hole superradiance in the presence of torsion within the framework of Poincaré gauge theory. In particular, in contrast to the classical approach of General Relativity, we show that the inclusion of torsion in the space-time geometry enables the energy extraction from rotating black holes by Dirac fermions via chiral asymmetry, while preserving the Pauli exclusion principle.

</details>

### [22] [Decay and structure of heavy flavour](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18098)
*Stefan Groote,Arpan Chatterjee,Maria Naeem*

Main category: hep-ph

TL;DR: This talk provides an overview of hadron physics research by the Tartu working group within the COST action CA24159, covering charmed baryon production/decays using current algebra and tensor invariants, CP violation via long-distance rescattering, neutron beta decay and polarized W boson decays using helicity formalism, identical-particle/mass effects in H→4ℓ, intrinsic charm discrepancies (SELEX vs. LHCb), and a nonlocal NJL+Faddeev framework for hadronic states.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To introduce collaborating groups to the Tartu working group's research scope within the COST action CA24159, bridging theoretical frameworks with experimental anomalies (e.g., SELEX–LHCb charm discrepancy) and open questions in hadron structure and spectroscopy.

Method: Current algebra with tensor invariants for charmed baryon decays; helicity formalism for neutron beta decay and polarized W decay; analysis of identical-particle statistics and mass effects in Higgs four-lepton decays; nonlocal field operators and nonlocal Nambu–Jona-Lasinio model derived from QCD, coupled with relativistic Faddeev equations for hadron description.

Result: Demonstrates applicability of current algebra + tensor invariants to CP-violating long-distance rescattering; shows helicity approach extends to electroweak radiative corrections; identifies role of quantum statistics/mass in H→4ℓ; proposes nonlocal operator-based resolution to intrinsic charm discrepancy; establishes nonlocal NJL+Faddeev as viable framework for hadronic states.

Conclusion: The Tartu group’s work integrates multiple theoretical tools across scales—from low-energy current algebra and chiral dynamics to nonlocal QCD-inspired models—highlighting interconnections between CP violation, decay dynamics, hadron structure, and open challenges for the COST action.

Abstract: In accordance to the aim of the constituing meeting of the COST action CA24159 ``Structure and Spectroscopy of Hadrons Research Project'' to introduce the different groups to the action, in this talk we give an overview over the subjects dealt with by the working group in Tartu related to hadron physics. We deal with the production and the nonleptonic decays of charmed baryons in the framework of the current algebra approach in terms of tensor invariants and explain how this approach can be used to approach CP violation via long distance effects in rescattering. New physics effects can be even seen in the classical neutron beta decay, but the helicity approach used here is also useful for e.g.\ calculating first order electroweak radiative corrections to the decay of the polarised $W$ boson. Identical particle and mass effects are seen in the Higgs decay into four leptons of the same type. The second main part starts with indications for the intrinsic charm mechanism, explaining the discrepancy between the results of SELEX and LHCb. The solution offered here is valid only if one considers nonlocal field operators. The nonlocal extension of the Nambu--Jona-Lasinio model, derived directly from QCD and combined with the relativistic Faddeev approach, allows for the description of hadronic states. We conclude by presenting open questions to the action.

Abstract: Thermal misalignment provides an alternative to the standard misalignment mechanism for the cosmological production of scalar dark matter. In this framework, feeble couplings to particles in the thermal bath generate a finite-temperature potential that drives the scalar towards large field values early in the radiation era, dynamically inducing the misalignment before the onset of scalar oscillations. As a result, the relic abundance is controlled primarily by particle masses and couplings rather than the initial field value. As a light spectator field, the scalar acquires inflationary fluctuations that are uncorrelated with the adiabatic curvature mode, generically sourcing isocurvature perturbations. We show that, unlike standard misalignment, where light scalars are strongly constrained by cosmic microwave background bounds on dark matter isocurvature for high-scale inflation, thermal misalignment can naturally suppress the isocurvature signal. This occurs through a novel late-time phase offset between the background zero mode and the superhorizon perturbations, which reduces the final dark matter density contrast. Thermal misalignment therefore provides a new and generic route to isocurvature-safe scalar dark matter.

The resummed results are consistently matched to fixed-order calculations up to $\mathcal{O}(α_S^3)$. Our resummation formalism also incorporates dominant heavy-quark mass effects and models non-perturbative power corrections by means of an analytic dispersive approach. A simultaneous fit yields an excellent description of experimental data across all energies, enabling a precise determination of the strong coupling, $α_S(m_Z^2) = 0.119 \pm 0.002$, as well as the non-perturbative parameters, including those characterizing the Collins--Soper evolution kernel. Our analysis includes, for the first time in a global fit, datasets from the ALEPH and AMY collaborations.

In this paper, we show how the Loop-Tree Duality (LTD) is particularly well suited for systematically identifying finite integrals, as it makes the origin of infrared and threshold singularities fully transparent at the integrand level. This clear separation of singular and non-singular contributions enables a more efficient strategy for isolating and promoting finite integrals, thereby streamlining both reduction and numerical evaluation. We present a new strategy based on numerator and raised propagator Ansätze that provides results similar to other methods, although in a clearer and compact way. While this construction and other approaches establish a robust foundation, they often produce integrands that exhibit a rapid growth in the ultraviolet (UV) regime. To mitigate this bad UV behaviour, we introduce a generalized set of integrands fully defined within LTD. This new set is inherently infrared-finite and frequently free of threshold singularities, offering a more versatile framework for high-order calculations.

The crossover is accompanied by a stretched ``string'' of proper co-dimensionality that confines the source to the domain wall. The effect takes place for different setups, such as phase transitions leading to confinement, both electric and magnetic, as well as in string theoretic inflation with $D$-branes. Our approach includes: (1) measuring azimuthal asymmetries of a collinear dihadron in semi-inclusive deep inelastic lepton scattering off an unpolarized proton target at the Electron-Ion Collider, and (2) utilizing azimuthal asymmetries of dihadron $(h_1 h_2)$ produced in association with an additional hadron $h^\prime$ at lepton colliders. These asymmetries provide a unique means to observe transversely polarized quarks, which arise from quantum interference and are exclusively sensitive to dipole interactions at the leading power of the new physics scale. Consequently, they exhibit a linear dependence on the dipole couplings, free from contamination by other new physics effects. This approach has the potential to significantly strengthen current constraints by one to two orders of magnitude. By combining all possible channels of $h^\prime$, this novel approach enables the disentanglement of the up- and down-quark dipole moments. Additionally, by controlling the electron's longitudinal polarization and the center-of-mass energy, it separates the contributions mediated by photon and weak boson. Furthermore, it allows for a simultaneous determination of both real and imaginary parts of the dipole couplings, offering a new avenue for investigating potential $CP$-violating effects at high energies.

TL;DR: This paper investigates pseudoscalar hidden-charm tetraquark states $Z_c^+$ and $Z_c^-$ using QCD sum rules and quark-hadron duality, computing their two-body strong decay widths via hadronic coupling constants derived from vacuum condensates up to dimension 5.

Result: Computed total decay widths: $Γ_{Z_c^-} = 326.197^{+4.255}_{-3.106}$ MeV and $Γ_{Z_c^+} = 91.835^{+0.96}_{-0.76}$ MeV, corresponding to $J^{PC}=0^{--}$ and $0^{-+}$ states with specified diquark-antidiquark configurations.

Conclusion: The significant difference in decay widths supports distinct internal structures for $Z_c^+$ and $Z_c^-$, validating the adopted diquark-antidiquark framework and providing quantitative predictions for experimental identification.

Abstract: In this work, we study the properties of the pseudoscalar hidden-charm tetraquark states by analyzing their two-body strong decays via the QCD sum rules based on rigorous quark-hadron duality. We take into account the vacuum condensates up to dimension 5 at the QCD side, and obtain the hadronic coupling constants. At last, we obtain the total decay widths $Γ_{Z_{c}^{-}} = 326.197^{+4.255}_{-3.106}$ MeV and $Γ_{Z_{c}^{+}} = 91.835^{+0.96}_{-0.76}$ MeV, respectively, where the $Z_{c}^{+}$($J^{PC}=0^{-+}$) and $Z_{c}^{-}$($J^{PC}=0^{--}$) denote the pseudoscalar hidden-charm tetraquarks with the diquark-antidiquark structures $[uc]_{A}[\bar{d}\bar{c}]_{V}-[uc]_{V}[\bar{d}\bar{c}]_{A}$ and $[uc]_{A}[\bar{d}\bar{c}]_{V}+[uc]_{V}[\bar{d}\bar{c}]_{A}$, respectively.

Furthermore, we study the correlation between bounds from meson decays and $μ\to e$ conversion. ### [54] [When do real observers resolve de Sitter's imaginary problem?](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18068)
*Ahmed Farag Ali*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: This paper analyzes how the universal phase factor i^{D+2} in the Euclidean de Sitter path integral impedes interpreting the Gibbons–Hawking entropy as a state count, and identifies a precise condition—shared negative modes with the conformal factor—under which certain 'real observers' can eliminate this phase.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To resolve the tension between the imaginary phase of the Euclidean de Sitter path integral and a statistical (state-counting) interpretation of the Gibbons–Hawking entropy, by clarifying when and why certain observers can render the path integral real.

Method: Analyzes the factorization structure of the gravitational path integral near the de Sitter saddle point; distinguishes gravitational observers from topological spectators; examines infrared effective actions for metric independence; uses SU(3) gauge theory and topological orders as concrete examples to test observer criteria involving clock functionality and negative-mode alignment with the conformal factor.

Result: A necessary and sufficient condition is derived: only observers whose quantum fluctuations include the negative modes associated with the conformal factor can eliminate the universal i^{D+2} phase; mere possession of an information-bearing clock is insufficient.

Conclusion: The Gibbons–Hawking entropy admits a state-counting interpretation only for a special class of 'real observers' defined by dynamical alignment with the conformal-factor instability—highlighting an intimate link between observer physics, gravitational path integral reality, and entropy interpretation.

Abstract: The universal phase $\rev{\ii}^{D+2}$ of the Euclidean de Sitter path integral obstructs a straightforward state-counting interpretation of the Gibbons--Hawking entropy. Building on Maldacena's proposal that specific black-hole observers can reorganize this phase, we derive a general constraint on when such ``real observers'' can succeed. By distinguishing \emph{gravitational observers} from \emph{topological spectators}, we show that any sector whose \emph{infrared effective} action is metric independent at the de Sitter saddle factorizes in the path integral, $\Ztot = \Zgrav^{(\text{obs})}\Ztop$, so the imaginary phase persists regardless of the sector's information-processing capabilities. Using confining $\SU(3)$ gauge theory and topological orders as examples, we demonstrate that an information-bearing clock is necessary but insufficient: only observers whose fluctuations share the negative modes of the conformal factor belong to the special class that can remove the de Sitter phase.

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To assess whether certain curvature singularities—arising in dynamical cobordisms and driving scalars to infinite distance in field space—should be physically acceptable or discarded, given tensions between existing singularity acceptability criteria and concrete string-theoretic examples like EFT strings and D7-branes.

Method: Analytical comparison of moduli-space flows and scalar potential-driven flows against Gubser's horizon and potential criteria and the Maldacena–Nuñez criterion; explicit uplift to consistent string backgrounds; examination of Klebanov–Tseytlin/Strassler solutions; derivation of near-extremal black Dp-brane reductions; proposal and validation of a new Ricci-scalar divergence bound as a geometric refinement of Gubser’s potential criterion.

Result: Moduli-space flows satisfy Gubser’s potential and Maldacena–Nuñez criteria but lack near-extremal horizons; EFT strings and D7-branes violate Gubser’s potential criterion despite UV completeness; a new Ricci-scalar-based criterion is formulated and shown to include those cases while excluding the massive IIA strong-coupling singularity; black Dp-brane reductions yield an exponential T ∝ exp(−Δφ) relation, suggesting a finite-temperature Distance Conjecture for dynamical cobordisms.

Conclusion: Codimension-one End-of-the-World singularities driving infinite field-space distance are not generically pathological; their physical acceptability depends on the nature of the infinite-distance limit and can be robustly assessed via the proposed Ricci-scalar divergence criterion, which unifies and extends prior criteria and supports a thermal generalization of the Swampland Distance Conjecture.

Abstract: We revisit codimension-one End-of-the-World curvature singularities that drive scalars to infinite distance in field-space and have appeared in the context of dynamical cobordisms. We confront them with Gubser's horizon and potential criteria and with the Maldacena--Nuñez criterion. Moduli-space flows do not admit a near-extremal horizon generalization. Still, they satisfy Gubser's potential criterion and, in representative string realizations, the Maldacena--Nuñez criterion in ten dimensions. Together with an explicit uplift of this type of solution to a consistent string theory background, this suggests that such singularities should not be discarded. For flows with non-trivial scalar potential, we argue that the fate of the singularity is tied to the infinite-distance limit probed near the singularity. The Klebanov--Tseytlin and Klebanov--Strassler solutions illustrate that a modification that obstructs or modifies the field excursion should not be understood as a UV-resolution of the original singularity. We show that EFT strings and D7-branes fail Gubser's potential criterion despite having a sensible UV completion. Motivated by this, and inspired by dynamical cobordisms, we propose a novel criterion that bounds the divergence of the Ricci scalar as the flow explores infinite distance in field-space. Our criterion can be viewed as a geometrization Gubser's one that, while capturing all examples accepted by the latter, also admits EFT strings and D7-branes. Both criteria reject the massive Type IIA strong coupling End-of-the-World singularity. Finally, we analyze black D$p$-branes reduced to codimension one as representatives of flows that admit near-extremal generalizations, and find an exponential relation between temperature and field-space distance. This suggests a finite-temperature extension of the Distance Conjecture for dynamical cobordisms.
