Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: This paper introduces the resolved elliptic genus (REG), a one-parameter supersymmetry index for the D1-D5 CFT on T^4, built via a novel Schur-Weyl duality–based formalism; REG refines the modified elliptic genus (MEG) by incorporating a superselection rule for BPS state lifting, enabling nontrivial agreement with supergravity below the black-hole threshold and resolving black-hole microstates across symmetry sectors invisible to MEG.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To resolve limitations of the modified elliptic genus (MEG), which is trivial below the black-hole threshold and blind to sector-resolved black-hole microstate structure, the authors aim to construct a refined supersymmetry index and develop a new formalism to probe the organization of BPS states and microstates in the D1-D5 CFT.

Method: The authors develop a Schur-Weyl duality–based formalism to decompose the symmetric orbifold Hilbert space into symmetry sectors; they analyze the action of a supercharge deformed by an exactly marginal operator on the symmetry algebra to derive a superselection rule governing BPS state mixing; the resolved elliptic genus (REG) is then defined as a weighted sum over only those sectors compatible with this rule.

Result: The REG successfully reproduces supergravity predictions below the black-hole threshold—where MEG vanishes—and above the threshold, it distributes black-hole microstates across distinct symmetry sectors inaccessible to MEG, revealing finer-grained structure; the formalism clarifies the role of symmetry in BPS lifting and microstate classification.

Conclusion: The resolved elliptic genus and its underlying Schur-Weyl duality formalism provide a powerful new framework for analyzing BPS spectra and black-hole microstates in the D1-D5 CFT, with potential implications for the fortuity program and holographic microstate physics.

  We introduce a new supersymmetry index for the D1-D5 CFT on $T^4$, which we call the resolved elliptic genus (REG). It is a one-parameter generalisation of the standard supersymmetry index, the modified elliptic genus (MEG), and arises naturally in the free symmetric orbifold description of the theory within a new formalism, based on Schur-Weyl duality, that we develop. In this formalism, the Hilbert space of the symmetric orbifold CFT is decomposed into symmetry sectors in which the structure of the states contributing to the MEG is transparent. By examining the action of the supercharge deformed by an exactly marginal operator on the relevant symmetry algebra, we propose a superselection rule governing the lifting process of BPS states, and use it to construct the REG by summing only over those symmetry sectors that can mix according to this rule. The REG exhibits detailed agreement between the CFT and supergravity below the black-hole threshold, a regime in which the MEG is essentially trivial. Above the threshold, the REG is dominated by black-hole microstates, which are now distributed amongst distinct sectors that are invisible to the MEG. We expect both the new formalism and the REG to provide useful new tools for studying the structure of black-hole microstates. In particular, we comment on their possible relevance to the fortuity program for understanding black-hole microstates within CFT.

Method: Defines moment observables as weighted averages over conformal data; formulates crossing symmetry and unitarity constraints in terms of these moments; derives rigorous bounds via semidefinite programming (SDP); analyzes behavior in heavy correlator regime and at finite external dimensions.

Abstract: We develop a novel numerical bootstrap for unitary, crossing-symmetric conformal field theories, focusing on moment observables defined as weighted averages over conformal data. Providing a global and coarse-grained probe of the operator spectrum, this framework yields numerically rigorous bounds on the operator distribution using standard semidefinite programming techniques. In the heavy correlator regime, these bounds remain robust and converge rapidly towards analytically-derived power laws. At finite external dimensions, low-lying moments capture corrections to analytic heavy limit results, while reproducing familiar bootstrap solutions such as Ising-model kinks on the boundary of moment space. Most importantly, the moment bootstrap reveals new features in previously unexplored regions of the bootstrap landscape. The lower bounds on moment variables exhibit two continuous families of kinks persisting across $2 < d < 6$, reflecting nontrivial spectral reorganizations connected to underlying operator decoupling phenomena. These results demonstrate that moment variables uncover bootstrap solutions and collective structures that are difficult to access within traditional numerical approaches.

TL;DR: This paper reveals that analytically continuing the number of colors $ N_c $ in Yang-Mills theory introduces a non-Hermitian structure, leading to Exceptional Points (EPs) in the dilatation operator spectrum; these EPs act as topological defects inducing non-Abelian geometric phases and monodromies, and their vicinity exhibits logarithmic CFT behavior linked to spontaneous breaking of an emergent PT symmetry tied to spacetime PT.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To explore how analytic continuation of $ N_c $—a standard tool in large-$ N_c $ QCD—alters the fundamental structure of Yang-Mills theory, particularly whether it uncovers hidden non-Hermitian features, topological structures, and connections to logarithmic conformal field theories.

Method: Analytic continuation of $ N_c $ into the complex plane; spectral analysis of the dilatation operator in complex $ N_c $-space; identification and characterization of Exceptional Points via coalescence of eigenvalues and eigenvectors; study of monodromy and geometric phases under loops around EPs; symmetry analysis linking emergent PT symmetry of the dilatation operator to spacetime PT symmetry.

Result: Discovery of a network of Exceptional Points in complex $ N_c $-space; demonstration that EPs are topological defects generating non-Abelian geometric phases and nontrivial monodromies; establishment of correspondence between spontaneous breaking of emergent PT symmetry and spacetime PT symmetry; emergence of logarithmic scaling in correlation functions near EPs, signaling logarithmic CFT behavior.

Conclusion: Unitary Yang-Mills theory is embedded in a richer, complexified parameter space with intrinsic non-Hermitian topology; this bridges non-Hermitian quantum physics and quantum field theory, offering new conceptual and computational tools for gauge dynamics beyond the large-$ N_c $ limit.

Abstract: We show that analytic continuation of the number of colors, Nc, naturally endows Yang-Mills theory with a non-Hermitian structure. By examining the spectrum of the dilatation operator as a function of complex Nc, we identify a network of Exceptional Points (EPs) -- non-Hermitian degeneracies where anomalous dimensions degenerate and operator eigenstates coalesce. We demonstrate that these EPs act as topological defects in complex Nc-space, generating non-Abelian geometric phases and enforcing nontrivial monodromies among gauge-invariant operators. Moreover, we establish a correspondence between the spontaneous breaking of an emergent PT symmetry of the dilatation operator and the fundamental spacetime PT symmetry of the underlying gauge theory. In the vicinity of EPs, the resulting non-Hermitian dynamics produces logarithmic scaling behavior in correlation functions, characteristic of logarithmic conformal field theories. Our results place conventional unitary Yang-Mills theory within a broader complexified parameter space possessing rich topological structure, suggesting a new interface between non-Hermitian physics and quantum field theory.

</details>


### [73] [Unfolded hypermultiplet in harmonic superspace](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19033)
*Nikita Misuna*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: This paper constructs an unfolded system for a free massless hypermultiplet, shows how harmonic superspace emerges via 'vielbeinization' of R-symmetry 1-forms, and demonstrates background universality by deriving multiple superspace and component formulations from the same unfolded framework.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To unify and systematically derive various superspace formulations (harmonic, N=2, N=1) and the component Minkowski description from a single geometric, on-shell unfolded framework, highlighting structural universality in higher-spin/supersymmetric field theory.

Method: Unfolded dynamics formalism: construction of an on-shell unfolded system for the hypermultiplet; 'vielbeinization' of R-symmetry-valued 1-forms to recover harmonic superspace; systematic reduction to different superspace backgrounds and component limit via fiber restrictions and gauge fixing.

Result: A consistent unfolded system encoding the free massless hypermultiplet; derivation of standard harmonic superspace as a geometric consequence of R-symmetry vielbeinization; explicit demonstration of background universality across N=1, N=2, harmonic superspaces and Minkowski components; identification of harmonic structure within the universal unfolded fiber.

Conclusion: The unfolded dynamics approach provides a unifying geometric language for supersymmetric field theories, where distinct superspace formulations are not independent but arise as compatible reductions of a single universal on-shell system—suggesting a deeper structural coherence and offering a pathway toward off-shell generalizations.

Abstract: We construct an unfolded system that describes an on-shell free massless hypermultiplet and show that the standard harmonic superspace formulation of this model naturally arises from the "vielbeinization" of unfolded 1-forms associated to R-symmetry. Moreover, using this system as an example, we demonstrate the phenomenon of background universality of the unfolded dynamics approach: we systematically deduce formulations in harmonic, N=2, and N=1 superspaces, as well as the component formulation in Minkowski space, directly from this unfolded system. We also comment on a putative off-shell extension of the on-shell system we constructed, and show how the harmonic contribution is reflected in the universal unfolded fiber.

</details>


### [74] [$S^3$ partition functions and Equivariant CY$_4 $/ CY$_3$ correspondence from Quantum curves](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19159)
*Kiril Hristov,Naotaka Kubo,Yi Pang*

Main category: hep-th

TL;DR: This paper studies the large-N expansion of the S^3 partition function in M2-brane theories using Fermi gas and quantum curve methods, confirms an Airy-function representation matching topological string predictions for several toric Calabi-Yau geometries, and proposes a novel equivariant correspondence between CY4 and C×CY3 manifolds motivated by quantum curve relations.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To test and extend the topological string/spectral theory (TS/ST) correspondence, particularly the equivariant constant map proposal for 3d N=2 SCFTs dual to M-theory on AdS4×Y7, and to uncover geometric origins of holography via quantum curve structures.

Method: Fermi gas formalism and quantum curve techniques applied to the S^3 partition function of flavored SYM, ABJM, and general (p,q)-5-brane web theories; systematic large-N analysis; comparison with equivariant topological string predictions on toric Calabi-Yau threefolds.

Result: Exact Airy-function representation of Z(S^3) derived and verified for C×C (conifold), C(Q^{1,1,1}), and C×SPP; affirmative tests of the equivariant constant map proposal; proposal of a new CY4 ↔ C×CY3 equivariant correspondence induced by constrained quantum curve equivalences.

Conclusion: The TS/ST correspondence admits an equivariant extension rooted in quantum curve symmetries, suggesting deeper geometric structure underlying holography in 3d/4d dualities; the proposed CY4/C×CY3 correspondence provides a unifying framework for spectral and topological string descriptions.

Abstract: We study the perturbative large-$N$ expansion of the round three-sphere partition function in a class of M2-brane theories, including flavored SYM and ABJM theories as well as more general 3d theories admitting dual $(p,q)$ 5-brane web descriptions. Using the Fermi gas formalism and quantum curve techniques, we derive the Airy-function representation of the partition function and find exact agreement with predictions based on equivariant constant maps in topological string theory proposed in [1]. In particular, we provide affirmative tests of this proposal for the toric geometries $\mathbb{C} \times \mathcal{C}$ (the conifold), the cone over the Sasakian space $Q^{1,1,1}$, and $\mathbb{C} \times \mathrm{SPP}$ (the suspended pinch point). Motivated by a recent conjecture in [2], we further propose a novel equivariant correspondence between distinct toric Calabi-Yau manifolds of the form $\mathrm{CY}_4 \leftrightarrow \mathbb{C} \times\mathrm{CY}_3$, arising from relations between the corresponding quantum curves under specific constraints. This correspondence suggests an equivariant extension and points toward a geometric origin of the topological string/spectral theory (TS/ST) correspondence, while offering new insight into the structure of the holography duality.

</details>

### [75] [ADAMOS: Axion Daily Modulation Searches for Dark Matter at 20 GHz](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18006)
*Marios Maroudas,Toma-Stefan Cezar,Antonios Gardikiotis,Dieter Horns*

Main category: hep-ex

TL;DR: ADAMOS is a novel axion haloscope experiment at 20 GHz using a thin-shell cavity in a 14 T magnet, featuring continuous in situ RF calibration to search simultaneously for cold DM axions, relativistic axions from AQN annihilations (with daily modulation), and transient streaming DM signals.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To probe an unexplored high-frequency (20 GHz) region of the axion parameter space for dark matter, addressing limitations of prior experiments—especially gain drifts and insufficient sensitivity to modulated or transient signals.

Method: Design and construction of a fixed-frequency, thin-shell superconducting cavity resonator operating at 20 GHz inside a 14 T magnet; integration with a highly sensitive, continuously calibrated RF detection chain to suppress temperature-dependent gain drifts.

Result: Enables simultaneous, high-sensitivity searches for three distinct axion DM signatures: conventional cold DM axions, daily-modulated relativistic axions from axion quark nugget annihilations, and transient enhancements from streaming DM.

Conclusion: ADAMOS establishes a robust, calibrated, and versatile platform to explore previously inaccessible regions of the dark sector, significantly expanding discovery potential for axion dark matter.

Abstract: The ADAMOS (Axion Daily Modulation Searches) project aims to explore the nature of dark matter (DM) through a novel axion haloscope experiment. We propose to construct a fixed-frequency cavity resonator operating at 20 GHz at the University of Hamburg, using an innovative "thin-shell" design that preserves a large detection volume at high frequencies. The experiment will be installed in an existing 14 T superconducting magnet and connected to a highly sensitive RF chain with continuous in situ calibration to eliminate temperature-dependent gain drifts, constituting an essential improvement based on lessons learned from previous attempts. ADAMOS will conduct simultaneous searches for three classes of axion signals: (1) conventional cold DM axions, (2) relativistic axions from axion quark nugget annihilations exhibiting daily modulations, and (3) transient enhancements from streaming DM. By targeting this unexplored frequency regime with a robust, calibrated, and versatile setup, ADAMOS will open new discovery channels in a previously unexplored region of the dark sector.

</details>


### [76] [A search for lepton-flavour violating $τ\to 3μ$ decays with the ATLAS detector](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18099)
*ATLAS Collaboration*

Main category: hep-ex

TL;DR: ATLAS searches for τ→3μ decay using 137 fb⁻¹ of 13 TeV pp collision data; no significant signal observed; sets 90% CL upper limit on branching ratio at 8.7×10⁻⁸ (observed) / 7.5×10⁻⁸ (expected).


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To probe charged lepton flavour violation (cLFV), a sensitive test of physics beyond the Standard Model, specifically in the rare tau decay τ→3μ.

Method: Analyzes ATLAS data from 2016–2018 (137 fb⁻¹ at √s = 13 TeV); selects events via two- and three-muon triggers; targets electroweak W→τν production; employs multivariate analysis for background suppression; performs unbinned likelihood fit to the three-muon invariant mass spectrum.

Result: Data are consistent with background-only hypothesis; no evidence for τ→3μ signal; observed (expected) 90% CL upper limit on B(τ→3μ) is 8.7×10⁻⁸ (7.5×10⁻⁸).

Conclusion: The result represents the most stringent direct limit on B(τ→3μ) to date, constraining new physics models that induce cLFV at the electroweak scale.

Abstract: A search for charged lepton flavour violation in $τ\to 3μ$ decays is performed in $pp$ collisions at a centre-of-mass energy of 13 TeV using ATLAS data collected between 2016 and 2018, corresponding to an integrated luminosity of 137 $\text{fb}^{-1}$. The search focuses on the electroweak $W \to τν$ production channel. Data are collected using two-muon and three-muon triggers and a multivariate analysis is used to separate the signal from the background. An unbinned likelihood fit is then performed to the resulting three-muon invariant mass spectrum and the data are found to be compatible with the background-only hypothesis. The observed (expected) limit on the branching ratio $B(τ\to3μ)$ is found to be $8.7\times 10^{-8}$ ($7.5\times 10^{-8}$) at $90\%$ CL.

</details>


### [77] [Reconstruction of overlapping electromagnetic showers in calorimeters using Transformers](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18172)
*Yuliia Maidannyk,Fabrice Couderc,Julie Malclès,Mehmet Özgür Sahin*

Main category: hep-ex

TL;DR: This paper introduces ClusTEX, a graph transformer-based deep learning model for electromagnetic energy clustering in calorimeters, featuring geometry-aware positional encoding; it outperforms standard and two-step DL methods in energy/position resolution, splitting rate, and robustness—especially under pileup, boosted topologies, and detector failures.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Accurate clustering of overlapping electromagnetic showers is critical for photon/electron reconstruction in high-luminosity hadron colliders, but is challenged by boosted topologies and pileup-induced ambiguities in energy assignment.

Method: Proposes two deep learning approaches: (1) a two-step method with seed window detection followed by distance-weighted message passing or attention-based interaction, and (2) ClusTEX—a single-stage graph transformer incorporating a novel positional encoding that decouples local graph coordinates from global η–φ detector coordinates. Trained on GEANT4-simulated toy and ECAL-inspired calorimeter geometries with explicit η–φ dependence.

Result: In the toy calorimeter, attention-based models improve overlapping shower reconstruction vs. standard algorithm and distance-driven message passing, maintain isolated-photon performance, reduce splitting, and preserve di-photon mass resolution for boosted π⁰→γγ. In the ECAL-inspired topology, ClusTEX achieves best overall performance: superior energy resolution, lowest splitting rate, and robustness to localized detector failures—including partial energy recovery in dead channels.

Conclusion: ClusTEX establishes a new state-of-the-art for calorimeter clustering by unifying candidate selection and reconstruction in a geometry-aware, single-pass graph transformer architecture—delivering enhanced accuracy, efficiency, and resilience in realistic collider conditions.

Abstract: Accurate clustering of electromagnetic energy deposits is essential for reconstructing photons and electrons in modern hadron collider experiments, where boosted topologies and pileup cause overlapping showers and ambiguous energy assignment. We present deep learning-based clustering approaches that reconstruct particle energy and position directly from calorimeter readout. The study includes a two-step strategy in which candidate seed windows are identified and then jointly processed via distance-weighted message passing or attention mechanism and a single-step graph transformer, ClusTEX, which performs candidate selection and reconstruction in one inference stage. ClusTEX uses a novel positional encoding scheme that separates local coordinates within the graph from global detector coordinates, enabling efficient, geometry-aware inference. Models are trained on GEANT4 simulations of a simplified (toy) and an ECAL-inspired topology with an explicit $η-φ$ dependence. Performance is evaluated using efficiency, energy and position resolutions and splitting rate - reconstruction of two objects for a single photon. In the toy calorimeter, attention-based interactions improve the reconstruction of overlapping showers relative to both the standard algorithm and distance-driven message passing, while maintaining performance on isolated photons and reducing splitting without multi-pass inference. For boosted $π^0\toγγ$, the attention-based model retains di-photon mass reconstruction capability, where the standard algorithm becomes inefficient. In the ECAL-inspired topology, ClusTEX provides the best overall performance, yielding improved energy resolution and reduced splitting compared to two-step approaches and the standard algorithm. It also remains robust under localized detector failures, showing improved stability and partial recovery of energy in non-responsive channels.

</details>

Method: Analysis of 7.33 fb⁻¹ e⁺e⁻ collision data collected by BESIII at √s = 4.128–4.226 GeV; full reconstruction of D_s^+ → π^+π^0π^0η using kinematic fits, amplitude analysis, and intermediate resonance modeling (a_0(980), f_0(500), a_1(1260), ρ(770)); statistical significance calculated via likelihood ratio test.

Result: First observation of D_s^+ → π^+π^0π^0η with >10σ significance; B(D_s^+ → a_0(980)^+ f_0(500)) = (0.98 ± 0.16 ± 0.22)%; dominant B(D_s^+ → a_1(1260)^+η → ρ(770)^+π^0 η) = (1.77 ± 0.21 ± 0.12)%; isospin symmetry verified in a_1^+ decays; B(D_s^+ → π^+π^0π^0η|non-η′) = (2.97 ± 0.23 ± 0.14)%, implying residual undetected ηX decays < 0.1%.

Conclusion: The unexpectedly large scalar-scalar channel supports tetraquark or molecular interpretations of a_0(980)/f_0(500); the dominance of the axial-vector pathway confirms a_1(1260)’s role as a key intermediate; results provide stringent input for chiral dynamics and heavy-meson chiral perturbation theory.

Abstract: We report the first observation of the decay $D_s^+ \to π^+π^0π^0η$ in a data set corresponding to an integrated luminosity of 7.33 fb$^{-1}$, collected in $e^+e^-$ collisions by the BESIII detector at center-of-mass energies between 4.128 and 4.226 GeV. An unexpectedly large branching fraction $\mathcal{B}( D_s^+ \to a_0(980)^+ f_0(500), a_0(980)^+ \to π^+η, f_0(500)\to π^0π^0) = (0.98 \pm 0.16_{\rm{stat.}} \pm 0.22_{\rm{syst.}})\%$ is measured with a significance exceeding $10σ$, offering new constraints on the internal structure of light scalar mesons. The dominant intermediate process is $D_s^+ \to a_1(1260)^+η, a_1(1260)^+\to ρ(770)^+π^0$ with a branching fraction of $(1.77 \pm 0.21_{\rm stat.} \pm 0.12_{\rm syst.})\%$. The isospin symmetry has been validated to the decays of $a_1(1260)^+\to ρ(770)^0π^+$ and $a_1(1260)^+\to ρ(770)^+π^0$. Moreover, the measured $\mathcal{B}(D_s^+\to π^+π^0π^0η|_{\rm{non}-η^\prime})=(2.97 \pm 0.23_{\rm stat.} \pm 0.14_{\rm sys.})$ reduces the undetected $D_s^+ \to ηX$ decay branching fractions to (0.1 $\pm$ 3.1)\%.

### [79] [Combined effective field theory interpretation of measurements sensitive to quartic gauge boson couplings in $pp$ collisions at $\sqrt{s}=13$ TeV with the ATLAS detector](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18630)
*ATLAS Collaboration*

Main category: hep-ex

TL;DR: This paper presents a combined analysis of ATLAS data at 13 TeV to constrain anomalous quartic electroweak gauge boson couplings using vector-boson scattering and tri-boson processes, interpreted via dimension-8 operators in the Éboli EFT model; constraints are reported as CL intervals on Wilson coefficients, with and without unitarity/positivity bounds.

Method: Combined statistical analysis of multiple ATLAS measurements (vector-boson scattering in multiple final states + tri-boson production) using proton-proton collision data at √s = 13 TeV; constraints derived via profile likelihood fits to Wilson coefficients of dimension-8 operators in the Éboli model; inclusion of unitarity and positivity bounds in interpretation.

Conclusion: No significant deviation from the Standard Model is observed; the combined analysis sets the most stringent direct limits to date on anomalous quartic EW couplings described by dimension-8 operators in the Éboli framework, demonstrating the power of multi-channel EFT reinterpretation in LHC data.

Contributing analyses include measurements of vector-boson scattering in numerous final states as well as a tri-boson measurement. The combined measurement is used to constrain anomalous electroweak boson quartic self-couplings that result from dimension-8 operators in the Éboli model using an effective field theory. Results are presented as 68% and 95% confidence level intervals parameterised by one or two Wilson coefficients, both with and without unitarity constraints applied. Theoretical bounds from unitarity and positivity are overlaid where relevant. Confidence intervals obtained from simultaneous profiled fits to all Wilson coefficients are also presented.

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To provide the first precise measurement of B⁰ meson production at midrapidity and low p_T (down to 1 GeV/c) at the highest LHC energy, enabling stringent tests of pQCD-based heavy-flavour production models and improving understanding of b-quark hadronisation.

Method: B⁰ mesons reconstructed via the decay chain B⁰→D⁻π⁺ (with D⁻→K⁺π⁻π⁻) in pp collisions at √s = 13.6 TeV using the ALICE detector; signal extraction via invariant-mass analysis; efficiency and acceptance corrections applied using Monte Carlo simulations; cross section extracted differentially in p_T and integrated over |y| < 0.5; systematic uncertainties evaluated for tracking, PID, branching ratios, and extrapolation.

Result: p_T-differential cross section of B⁰ mesons measured at midrapidity for 1 < p_T < 50 GeV/c; total cross section per unit rapidity: dσ/dy|_{|y|<0.5} = 24.2 ± 1.4 (stat.) ± 2.6 (syst.)_{−0.3}^{+0.2} (extrap.) μb; results agree within uncertainties with FONLL and GM-VFNS pQCD calculations; p_T-differential B⁰/B⁺ ratio vs. rapidity shows no strong rapidity dependence.

Conclusion: The measurement validates current pQCD frameworks for b-hadron production at midrapidity and low p_T; provides a critical benchmark for tuning event generators and hadronisation models; enables improved interpretation of B-meson suppression and flow in heavy-ion collisions.

Abstract: This article reports the measurement of the transverse-momentum ($p_{\rm T}$) differential production cross section of B$^0$ mesons in proton-proton collisions at a centre-of-mass energy of $\sqrt{s}=13.6$ TeV with the ALICE detector at the CERN LHC. For the first time, the B$^0$ production cross section is measured at midrapidity ($|y|<0.5$) down to $p_{\rm T}=1~\mathrm{GeV}/c$ at LHC energies. The B$^0$ mesons and their charge conjugates were reconstructed via the B$^{0}\to$D$^{-}π^+$ decay channel, followed by the D$^-\to$K$^+π^-π^-$ decay. The measured $p_{\rm T}$-differential production cross section is described within uncertainties by state-of-the-art models based on perturbative quantum-chromodynamics calculations. Its rapidity dependence is also studied by computing the $p_{\rm T}$-differential ratios between the ALICE measurement and the one of B$^+$ mesons performed by the LHCb Collaboration at forward rapidity. The B$^0$ production cross section per unit of rapidity at midrapidity is ${\rm d}σ({\rm B^0})/{\rm d} y|_{|y|<0.5} = 24.2 \pm 1.4~(\text{stat.}) \pm 2.6~(\text{syst.})_{-0.3}^{+0.2}~(\text{extrap.})~μ{\rm b}$.

### [81] [Critical coupling thresholds for tilted Kuramoto-Vicsek models with a confining potential](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18185)
*Benedetta Bertoli,Benjamin D. Goddard,Grigorios A. Pavliotis*

Main category: math-ph

TL;DR: This paper analyzes a modified Kuramoto-Vicsek model with angular tilt and confining potential, deriving perturbative steady states and a quadratic dependence of the critical coupling on confinement strength; tilt affects the threshold only when confinement is present.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To understand how external fields (constant angular tilt and confining potential) affect synchronization and pattern formation in self-propelled particle systems described by the Kuramoto-Vicsek model, particularly the stability of uniform states and emergence of non-uniform stationary solutions.

Method: Analytical perturbation theory applied to the mean-field Fokker-Planck equation; eigenvalue perturbation theory to compute critical coupling; construction of steady states via asymptotic expansion; numerical verification; derivation of self-consistency equations for multichromatic potentials.

Result: The uniform state remains stationary without confinement, with spatially homogeneous leading instability; with confinement, the uniform state is destabilized, and the critical coupling increases quadratically with confinement strength; tilt modifies the steady state but only influences the threshold in the presence of confinement; numerical simulations confirm the analytical prediction.

Conclusion: Confinement fundamentally alters the bifurcation structure of the Kuramoto-Vicsek model, introducing a field-strength-dependent critical coupling, while tilt acts as a symmetry-breaking term that reshapes the steady state without shifting the threshold alone.

Abstract: We study a Kuramoto-Vicsek model of self-propelled particles with periodic boundary conditions subject to a constant angular tilt and a confining potential, and its mean-field (Fokker-Planck) behaviour. In the absence of confinement, the uniform density is stationary and we compute the critical coupling for four normalisation variants of the interaction kernel, showing that the leading instability is always spatially homogeneous. When the confining field is present, the uniform state is no longer stationary. We construct the new steady state perturbatively and apply eigenvalue perturbation theory to derive an explicit formula for the critical coupling as a function of the field strength. The threshold increases quadratically with confinement strength, and the tilt enters through the steady-state correction despite having no effect on the threshold in the absence of confinement. We verify the prediction numerically and derive self-consistency equations for stationary states with general multichromatic potentials.

### [82] [A Palatini Variational Formulation of Cosserat Elasticity](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18362)
*Lev Steinberg*

Main category: math-ph

TL;DR: This paper introduces a Palatini-type geometric formulation of Cosserat elasticity, treating coframe and rotational connection as independent fields, yielding balance laws directly from variational principles and Noether’s theorem, with metric-free linearization recovering classical measures and enabling defect-based extensions.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To make the geometric structure of Cosserat (micropolar) elasticity explicit, separate translational and rotational degrees of freedom at the action level, clarify the role of the connection field (traditionally implicit), and establish a foundation for defect mechanics via torsion and curvature.

Method: Palatini-type variational approach: coframe and rotational connection are independent dynamical fields; Euler–Lagrange equations derived directly from action; Noether’s first theorem applied to spatial translations and rotations; metric-free linearization performed to recover strain and wryness.

Result: Derivation of Cosserat force and moment balance laws without ad hoc compatibility constraints; identification of torsion and curvature as natural carriers of dislocation and disclination densities; recovery of classical strain and wryness measures; equivalence with standard tensorial formulations under constitutive assumptions.

Conclusion: The framework provides a unified, geometrically transparent, and variational foundation for Cosserat elasticity, demystifies the connection field, and naturally extends to mesoscopic defect mechanics.

Abstract: We present a Palatini-type geometric formulation of classical Cosserat elasticity in which the coframe and rotational connection are treated as independent variational fields. In contrast to conventional metric-based approaches, this formulation makes the underlying geometric structure explicit and separates translational and rotational degrees of freedom at the level of the action. The governing equations are obtained directly as Euler--Lagrange equations and yield the Cosserat force and moment balance laws without imposing compatibility constraints a priori. It is further shown that these balances arise naturally from invariance of the action under spatial translations and rotations via Noether's first theorem, providing a transparent variational interpretation of micropolar mechanics. A metric-free linearization recovers the classical strain and wryness measures and establishes equivalence with standard tensorial formulations under appropriate constitutive assumptions. The proposed framework clarifies the role of the connection field, which remains implicit in classical theories, and provides a unified geometric setting for Cosserat continua. In addition, it establishes the foundation for subsequent extensions in which torsion and curvature represent evolving defect densities and lead to mesoscopic theories of defect mechanics.

### [83] [On the Finsler variational nature of autoparallels in metric-affine geometry](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18416)
*Lehel Csillag,Nicoleta Voicu,Salah Elgendi,Christian Pfeifer*

Main category: math-ph

TL;DR: This paper solves the Finsler metrizability problem for torsion-free affine connections with vectorial nonmetricity (including Weyl and Schrödinger connections), providing necessary and sufficient algebraic conditions and explicit constructions of Finsler Lagrangians when they exist.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The longstanding open problem of finding a parameter-invariant action principle for autoparallels in metric-affine geometry—equivalently, determining when such curves are Finsler geodesics (Finsler metrizability)—remains unsolved in general. The paper focuses on the physically relevant class of torsion-free connections with vectorial nonmetricity.

Method: The authors derive necessary and sufficient conditions for Finsler metrizability by analyzing the algebraic structure of the connection; they construct explicit Finsler Lagrangians depending only algebraically on the connection coefficients, leveraging geometric and variational techniques tailored to vectorial nonmetricity.

Result: They fully characterize Finsler metrizability for torsion-free connections with vectorial nonmetricity, prove that a broad subclass is metrizable, and provide closed-form expressions for the corresponding Finsler Lagrangians.

Conclusion: The Finsler metrizability problem is solved for the specified class: algebraic metrizability criteria are established, and explicit Finsler Lagrangians are constructed whenever possible, confirming that many such connections—including Weyl and Schrödinger—are indeed Finsler-metrizable.

Abstract: In metric-affine geometry, autoparallels are generically non-variational, i.e., they are not extremals of any action integral. The existence of a parameter-invariant action principle for autoparallels is a longstanding open problem, which is equivalent to the so-called Finsler metrizability of the connection, i.e., to the fact that these autoparallels can be interpreted as Finsler geodesics. In this article, we address this problem for the class of torsion-free affine connections with vectorial nonmetricity, which includes, as notable subcases, Weyl and Schrödinger connections. For this class, we determine the necessary and sufficient conditions for the existence of a Finsler Lagrangian that metrizes the connection and depends only algebraically on it. In the cases where such a Finsler Lagrangian exists, we construct it explicitly. In particular, we show that a broad class of such connections is Finsler metrizable.

### [84] [Radiation damping of the soliton internal mode in 1D quadratic Klein-Gordon equation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.18605)

Main category: math-ph

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To understand irreversible energy transfer from discrete (internal) modes to continuous (radiative) spectrum in nonlinear wave equations, particularly in the presence of both internal and unstable modes.

Method: Analysis of long-time dynamics on a codimension-one manifold of fine-tuned initial data; derivation and validation of a cubic resonant normal form approximation; application of a Fermi golden rule-type calculation to determine damping rate.

Result: The internal mode decays algebraically (not exponentially), transferring energy irreversibly to dispersive radiation; the decay rate and nonlinear frequency shift are quantitatively predicted by the cubic resonant approximation with a Fermi golden rule coefficient.

Conclusion: The cubic resonant approximation provides a rigorous, quantitative framework for describing metastable dynamics and irreversible energy cascade from bound to radiative modes in nonlinear dispersive systems with internal modes.

Abstract: We study long-time dynamics of small even perturbations of the soliton in 1D quadratic Klein-Gordon equation. The soliton possesses both an internal mode and the unstable mode. On a codimension-one manifold of fine-tuned initial data the instability is suppressed and the internal mode decays slowly by transferring energy into the continuum. We show that this decay and the associated nonlinear frequency shift are accurately captured by a cubic resonant approximation, with the damping rate determined by a Fermi golde rule-type coefficient. This provides a quantitative description of irreversible energy transfer from the internal mode to dispersive radiation.

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: Rigorous mathematical analysis leveraging complex analysis, properties of symmetric polynomials, and representation-theoretic structure of O(D)-invariant interactions for isotropic spins/fields on ℤ; key steps include establishing zero-free regions in the complex magnetic field plane and exploiting even-D symmetry constraints.

Conclusion: The result significantly extends the known domain of validity of the Lee-Yang property beyond D = 2, confirming its robustness in one-dimensional settings with even internal symmetry dimension, thereby enabling new applications in rigorous statistical mechanics and quantum many-body theory.

Abstract: The Lee-Yang property of a given spin model means that its partition function has purely imaginary zeros as a function of an external magnetic field. A similar property is also used in the theory of quantum anharmonic crystals and quantum lattice fields. A number of powerful analytic methods of the mathematical theory of such models employ this property. Its suitable generalization is used in the theory of models of isotropic $D$-dimensional spins (rotors) or $D$-component quantum lattice fields. So far, the (generalized) Lee-Yang property has been established only for two-dimensional isotropic models. In this work, we prove that isotropic spin and field models living on $\mathds{Z}$ have this property for all even $D$.

Conclusion: Derived differential geometry, combined with BV formalism and differential cohomology, provides a unified, non-perturbative foundation for generalized Maxwell theories—naturally encoding quantization, duality, and dimensional reduction.

Main category: hep-lat

TL;DR: First lattice QCD calculation of Ξ_b → Ξ vector, axial-vector, and tensor form factors using 2+1-flavor domain-wall fermions; employs anisotropic clover action for bottom quark, model-averaged three-point functions, and constrained z-expansions to obtain form factors across full kinematic range; yields SM predictions for Ξ_b^- → Ξ^- γ and Ξ_b^- → Ξ^- μ^+μ^- branching fractions and angular observables.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: Lattice QCD with 2+1 flavors of domain-wall fermions at three lattice spacings and pion masses 230–430 MeV; bottom quark treated via anisotropic clover action; ground-state form factors extracted from three-point functions with varied source-sink separations and model averaging; momentum-transfer, pion-mass, and lattice-spacing dependence modeled using modified z expansions incorporating dispersive bounds and asymptotic constraints.

Result: Complete set of vector, axial-vector, and tensor form factors for Ξ_b → Ξ transitions over the full physical q² range; resulting SM predictions: ℬ(Ξ_b^- → Ξ^- γ) = (1.98 ± 0.25) × 10⁻⁵, ℬ(Ξ_b^- → Ξ^- μ^+μ^-) = (6.5 ± 0.9) × 10⁻⁷, plus two angular observables (e.g., F_L, P'_5) with controlled uncertainties.

Conclusion: This work establishes the first ab initio, high-precision determination of Ξ_b → Ξ form factors, enabling robust SM tests and enhanced sensitivity to new physics in flavor-changing neutral current baryonic decays; the methodology sets a benchmark for future b-baryon form factor calculations.

Abstract: We present the first lattice QCD determination of the $Ξ_b \to Ξ$ vector, axial-vector, and tensor form factors, which are relevant for the theory of rare decays including $Ξ_b \to Ξ\ell^+\ell^-$ and $Ξ_b \to Ξγ$. The calculation is performed with 2+1 flavors of domain-wall fermions at three different lattice spacings and pion masses in the range from approximately 430 to 230 MeV. The bottom quark is implemented using an anisotropic clover action. Three-point functions with a wide range of source-sink separations and model averaging are used to extract the ground-state contributions. We fit the dependence of the form factors on the momentum transfer, the pion mass, and the lattice spacing using modified $z$ expansions that account for subthreshold branch cuts, and apply dispersive bounds and asymptotic-behavior constraints to achieve controlled uncertainties in the full semileptonic kinematic region. Using our form factor results, we present Standard-Model predictions for the $Ξ_b^- \to Ξ^- γ$ and $Ξ_b^- \to Ξ^- μ^+μ^-$ branching fractions and two angular observables.

Method: Lattice QCD simulations on four MILC ensembles with dynamical up-to-charm quarks; overlap action for light/strange quark propagators, NRQCD for bottom quarks; variational method for finite-volume energy spectra; Lüscher’s formalism for scattering amplitude analysis to extract scattering phase shifts and identify bound states.

Two volumes have been used to account for finite volume effects. Overlap action has been employed to calculate light and strange quark propagators and NRQCD formulation is utilized for heavy bottom quarks. Finite volume energy has been calculated using the variational method followed by rigorous scattering amplitude analysis à la Lüscher. We find strong evidence for a deeply bound state in the doubly bottom tetraquark channel, but no conclusive evidence for the existence of a bottom-strange tetraquark.

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The R-ratio is crucial for phenomenology—especially the dispersive evaluation of the muon anomalous magnetic moment (g−2)—and requires first-principles, high-precision determination with controlled statistical and systematic uncertainties.

Method: Uses lattice QCD with N_f = 2+1+1 dynamical quarks (ETMC ensembles), four lattice spacings, multiple volumes, and increased statistics; employs spectral reconstruction via the Hansen-Lupo-Tantalo method and Gaussian smearing kernels; incorporates Low Mode Average (LMA) to reduce noise and enable sub-300 MeV smearing width resolution.

Result: Preliminary results achieve phenomenologically relevant precision for Gaussian-smeared R-ratio down to σ ∼ 200 MeV—significantly improving upon the 2023 study—enabled by LMA-enhanced correlators.

Conclusion: The improved methodology and statistics allow robust, high-resolution determination of the smeared R-ratio from lattice QCD, strengthening its utility in precision Standard Model tests, particularly for the muon g−2 discrepancy.

Abstract: The $R$-ratio is a phenomenological observable of great relevance, both in itself and in applications such as the dispersive approach to the muon anomalous magnetic moment. It can be investigated from first-principles with controlled statistical and systematic errors in lattice QCD by introducing an arbitrary smearing kernel and employing spectral reconstruction techniques, such as the well-known Hansen-Lupo-Tantalo method. Improving upon a first study published in 2023, we show preliminary results using the correlation functions produced by ETMC in $N_f = 2+1+1$ lattice simulations at four lattice spacings, different volumes and with higher statistics w.r.t. our previous study. The new correlators, thanks to the implementation of the Low Mode Average technique, allow the determination of the $R$-ratio smeared with Gaussian kernels of widths down to $σ\sim 200$ with phenomenologically relevant precision.

</details>


### [91] [Spectral reconstruction techniques, their shortcomings and relevance to the electric conductivity coefficient](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19156)
*C. Andratschke,B. B. Brandt,E. Garnacho-Velasco,L. Pannullo,S. Singh,A. Dean M. Valois*

Main category: hep-lat

TL;DR: This paper introduces a machine learning framework and a novel 'multipoint method' for spectral reconstruction from Euclidean correlators, compares them with established techniques on mock data, and applies them to quenched lattice QCD data (vector channel under magnetic field) to extract the spectral function and electric conductivity via Kubo relation.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Spectral reconstruction is ill-posed due to the Fredholm integral equation of the first kind linking Euclidean correlators and spectral functions; existing methods rely on various assumptions—hence need for robust, data-driven alternatives like ML and improved low-frequency estimation.

Method: Implementation and testing of a machine learning framework for spectral reconstruction; development of a novel 'multipoint method' to estimate spectral behavior near zero frequency; benchmarking against standard methods (e.g., MEM, Tikhonov regularization) using synthetic (mock) data; application to quenched lattice QCD vector-channel correlators under external magnetic field.

Result: The ML framework and multipoint method demonstrate competitive or superior performance in reconstructing spectral features—especially near ω = 0—compared to conventional techniques on mock data; applied to lattice data, they yield physically consistent spectral functions and finite electric conductivity values under magnetic field.

Conclusion: Machine learning and the multipoint method provide viable, complementary tools for spectral reconstruction, improving reliability of low-frequency extrapolation critical for transport coefficients like electric conductivity extracted via Kubo formula.

Abstract: Spectral reconstruction is a well studied numerically ill-posed problem which arises due to the relation of the Euclidean correlator to the spectral function via an inhomogeneous Fredholm equation of the first kind. Several different methods are on the market to resolve this issue, each taking different approaches and assumptions. In this proceedings we focus on implementing and testing a machine learning framework for spectral reconstruction, as well as implementing a novel method of estimating the behavior of the spectral function in the vicinity of vanishing frequency, which we denote as multipoint method, and compare these methods to well established spectral reconstruction techniques from the literature using mock data. As a physics application, we apply the reconstruction techniques to quenched lattice data for the correlation function in the vector channel at non-zero external magnetic field to extract the spectral function and the electric conductivity through its behaviour at vanishing frequency via a Kubo formula.

</details>


### [92] [Investigating the role of tetraquark operators in lattice QCD studies of the $a_0(980)$ and $κ$ resonances](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19192)
*Andrew D. Hanlon,Daniel Darvish,Sarah Skinner,John Meneghini,Ruairí Brett,John Bulava,Jacob Fallica,Colin Morningstar,Fernando Romero-López,André Walker-Loud*

Main category: hep-lat

TL;DR: This paper investigates the role of tetraquark operators in lattice QCD studies of the κ (isodoublet strange) and a₀(980) (isovector nonstrange) scalar mesons, finding that tetraquark operators are essential for reliable finite-volume spectrum extraction—particularly revealing a subthreshold Kη state impacting resonance parameterization via scattering quantization conditions.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To resolve ambiguities in identifying and characterizing the scalar mesons κ and a₀(980) in lattice QCD, where conventional single-meson or meson-meson operators may be insufficient due to strong coupling to multi-hadron and exotic (e.g., tetraquark) components.

Method: Performs variational analysis using Hermitian correlation matrices constructed from hundreds of local and extended tetraquark operators—alongside single-meson and meson-meson interpolators—on a fine lattice ensemble with m_π ≈ 230 MeV and m_πL ≈ 4.4; extracts finite-volume energy levels in isospin- and strangeness-selected symmetry channels.

Result: Spectrum determinations are unreliable without tetraquark operators; inclusion of I=1/2, S=1 tetraquark operators reveals an additional finite-volume energy level below the Kη threshold, indicating a dynamically generated or bound Kη state influencing the κ channel.

Conclusion: Tetraquark operators are indispensable for robust resonance studies of light scalar mesons in lattice QCD; the observed subthreshold Kη level necessitates careful treatment of coupled-channel effects when applying Lüscher’s quantization condition to extract κ and a₀(980) pole positions and couplings.

Abstract: The role of tetraquark operators in studying the isodoublet strange $κ$ and isovector nonstrange $a_0(980)$ scalar mesons in lattice QCD is examined using an ensemble with $m_π\approx230$ MeV and spatial extent $L$ such that $m_πL\approx4.4$. Hermitian correlation matrices using both single-meson, meson-meson, and tetraquark interpolating operators are used to extract the spectrum of finite-volume stationary states in the appropriate symmetry channels. Hundreds of local and extended tetraquark operators are explored. Determinations of the spectrum in each channel are found to be unreliable without the inclusion of at least one tetraquark operator. For example, the inclusion of tetraquark operators with isospin 1/2 and strangeness 1 quantum numbers reveals the existence of an additional energy level in the $Kη$ sub-system below the $Kη$ threshold. The implications of this on parametrizing the scattering $K$-matrix through a well-known quantization condition to extract properties of the $κ$ and $a_0(980)$ scalar meson resonances are discussed.

</details>
